Question: 5 horses are in a race. Mr.Jain selects two of horses at random and bets on them. The probability that he selected the winning horse is # Answer option: ['A)1/5', 'B)2/5', 'C)3/5', 'D)4/5', 'E)6/5']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the probability that Mr. Jain selects the winning horse when he randomly selects two horses out of the five in the race.

1. **Total number of ways to select two horses from five:**
The number of ways to choose 2 horses out of 5 is given by the combination formula \( \binom{n}{r} \), where \( n \) is the total number of items to choose from, and \( r \) is the number of items to choose. So, we have:
\[
\binom{5}{2} = \frac{5 \times 4}{2 \times 1} = 10
\]
There are 10 possible pairs of horses that Mr. Jain can select.

2. **Number of favorable outcomes:**
For Mr. Jain to have selected the winning horse, the winning horse must be one of the two horses he selects. There are 5 horses, and only 1 of them is the winning horse. Once the winning horse is selected, Mr. Jain can choose any of the remaining 4 horses to complete his pair. Thus, there are 4 favorable outcomes (one for each of the other horses paired with the winning horse).

3. **Probability calculation:**
The probability that Mr. Jain selects the winning horse is the number of favorable outcomes divided by the total number of possible outcomes:
\[
\text{Probability} = \frac{\text{Number of favorable outcomes}}{\text{Total number of outcomes}} = \frac{4}{10} = \frac{2}{5}
\]

Therefore, the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse is \(\frac{2}{5}\).

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: Silu and Meenu were walking on the road. Silu said, "I weigh 51 Kgs. How much do you weigh?" Meenu replied that she wouldn't reveal her weight directly as she is overweight. But she said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight." How much does Meenu weigh? # Answer option: ['A)12', 'B)28', 'C)27', 'D)58', 'E)91']
To solve the problem, we need to determine Meenu's weight based on the information she provided. Let's break it down step by step:

1. Meenu said, "I weigh 29 Kgs plus half of my weight." Let's denote Meenu's weight as \( W \).

2. According to Meenu's statement, we can set up the equation:
\[
W = 29 + \frac{1}{2}W
\]

3. To solve for \( W \), we first need to eliminate the fraction. We can do this by multiplying every term in the equation by 2 to get rid of the fraction:
\[
2W = 58 + W
\]

4. Next, we subtract \( W \) from both sides to isolate \( W \) on one side of the equation:
\[
2W - W = 58
\]

5. Simplifying the left side gives:
\[
W = 58
\]

Therefore, Meenu weighs 58 Kgs.

The correct answer is option D.

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: Three bells ring at intervals of 36 seconds, 40 seconds and 48 seconds, respectively. They start ringing together at a particular time. When they will ring together again? # Answer option: ['A)After 6 minutes', 'B)After 12 minutes', 'C)After 18 minutes', 'D)After 24 minutes', 'E)none']
To determine when the three bells will ring together again, we need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of the intervals at which they ring. The intervals are 36 seconds, 40 seconds, and 48 seconds.

**Step 1: Prime Factorization**

- 36 can be factored into prime numbers as:
\(36 = 2^2 \times 3^2\)

- 40 can be factored into prime numbers as:
\(40 = 2^3 \times 5\)

- 48 can be factored into prime numbers as:
\(48 = 2^4 \times 3\)

**Step 2: Determine the LCM**

To find the LCM, take the highest power of each prime number that appears in the factorizations:

- The highest power of 2 is \(2^4\).
- The highest power of 3 is \(3^2\).
- The highest power of 5 is \(5^1\).

Thus, the LCM is:
\[ LCM = 2^4 \times 3^2 \times 5^1 \]

**Step 3: Calculate the LCM**

\[ LCM = 16 \times 9 \times 5 \]

First, calculate \(16 \times 9\):
\[ 16 \times 9 = 144 \]

Then, multiply the result by 5:
\[ 144 \times 5 = 720 \]

So, the LCM of 36, 40, and 48 is 720 seconds.

**Step 4: Convert Seconds to Minutes**

Since 1 minute = 60 seconds, convert 720 seconds to minutes:
\[ 720 \div 60 = 12 \]

Therefore, the three bells will ring together again after 12 minutes.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: A box contains a certain number of balls, marked successively from 1 to n. If there are 45 different ways that two balls can be selected from the box such that the ball with number 3 marked on it is not selected, then what is the value of n? # Answer option: ['A)11', 'B)10', 'C)9', 'D)8', 'E)7']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the value of \( n \) such that there are 45 different ways to select two balls from a box of \( n \) balls, excluding the ball marked with the number 3.

First, let's calculate the total number of ways to select 2 balls from \( n \) balls. This is given by the combination formula:

\[
\binom{n}{2} = \frac{n(n-1)}{2}
\]

However, we are given that the ball marked with the number 3 is not selected. This means we are selecting 2 balls from the remaining \( n-1 \) balls (since we exclude the ball marked with 3).

The number of ways to select 2 balls from \( n-1 \) balls is:

\[
\binom{n-1}{2} = \frac{(n-1)(n-2)}{2}
\]

According to the problem, this number is equal to 45:

\[
\frac{(n-1)(n-2)}{2} = 45
\]

To find \( n \), we solve the equation:

\[
(n-1)(n-2) = 90
\]

Expanding the left side, we have:

\[
n^2 - 3n + 2 = 90
\]

Rearranging gives:

\[
n^2 - 3n - 88 = 0
\]

This is a quadratic equation, which we can solve using the quadratic formula:

\[
n = \frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}
\]

where \( a = 1 \), \( b = -3 \), and \( c = -88 \). Plugging in these values:

\[
n = \frac{-(-3) \pm \sqrt{(-3)^2 - 4 \cdot 1 \cdot (-88)}}{2 \cdot 1}
\]

\[
n = \frac{3 \pm \sqrt{9 + 352}}{2}
\]

\[
n = \frac{3 \pm \sqrt{361}}{2}
\]

\[
n = \frac{3 \pm 19}{2}
\]

This gives two possible solutions:

\[
n = \frac{3 + 19}{2} = 11
\]

\[
n = \frac{3 - 19}{2} = -8
\]

Since \( n \) must be a positive integer, we have \( n = 11 \).

Thus, the value of \( n \) is 11. Therefore, the final answer is:

\[
\text{Final answer:} \{A\}
\]
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: x men working x hours per day can do x units of a work in x days. How much work can be completed by y men working y hours per day in y days? # Answer option: ['A)x2/y2 units', 'B)y3/x2 units', 'C)x3/y2 units', 'D)y2/x2 units', 'E)None of these']
To solve this problem, we need to understand the relationship between the number of men, the number of hours they work per day, the number of days they work, and the amount of work completed.

Given:
- \( x \) men working \( x \) hours per day can complete \( x \) units of work in \( x \) days.

From this, we can determine the total amount of work done in terms of man-hours:
- Total man-hours required to complete \( x \) units of work = \( x \) men \(\times\) \( x \) hours/day \(\times\) \( x \) days = \( x^3 \) man-hours.

This means \( x^3 \) man-hours are needed to complete \( x \) units of work. Therefore, the work done per man-hour is:
- Work per man-hour = \( \frac{x}{x^3} = \frac{1}{x^2} \) units of work per man-hour.

Now, we need to find out how much work \( y \) men working \( y \) hours per day can complete in \( y \) days.

Calculate the total man-hours available with \( y \) men:
- Total man-hours = \( y \) men \(\times\) \( y \) hours/day \(\times\) \( y \) days = \( y^3 \) man-hours.

Since each man-hour can complete \( \frac{1}{x^2} \) units of work, the total work completed by \( y^3 \) man-hours is:
- Total work = \( y^3 \) man-hours \(\times\) \( \frac{1}{x^2} \) units/man-hour = \( \frac{y^3}{x^2} \) units.

Thus, the amount of work that can be completed by \( y \) men working \( y \) hours per day in \( y \) days is \( \frac{y^3}{x^2} \) units.

Therefore, the correct answer is option B.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: A company produces 420 units of a particular computer component every month, at a production cost to the company of $110 per component, and sells all of the components by the end of each month. What is the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee that the yearly profit (revenue from sales minus production costs) will be at least $626,400? # Answer option: ['A)226', 'B)230', 'C)240', 'D)260', 'E)280']
To determine the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee a yearly profit of at least $626,400, we need to follow these steps:

1. **Calculate the Total Yearly Production Cost:**
- The company produces 420 units per month.
- The production cost per component is $110.
- Therefore, the monthly production cost is \( 420 \times 110 = 46,200 \) dollars.
- The yearly production cost is \( 46,200 \times 12 = 554,400 \) dollars.

2. **Determine the Required Yearly Revenue:**
- The yearly profit must be at least $626,400.
- Profit is calculated as Revenue - Production Costs.
- Therefore, the required yearly revenue is \( 626,400 + 554,400 = 1,080,800 \) dollars.

3. **Calculate the Required Monthly Revenue:**
- Since the company sells all components produced each month, the monthly revenue must be \( \frac{1,080,800}{12} = 90,066.67 \) dollars.

4. **Determine the Minimum Selling Price per Component:**
- The company sells 420 components each month.
- To achieve the required monthly revenue, the selling price per component must be \( \frac{90,066.67}{420} \approx 214.44 \) dollars.

5. **Select the Minimum Selling Price from the Options:**
- The options provided are: A) 226, B) 230, C) 240, D) 260, E) 280.
- The minimum selling price that is greater than or equal to $214.44 is $226.

Therefore, the minimum selling price per component that will guarantee the required yearly profit is option A) 226.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: One gram of a certain health food contains 9 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin E and 8 percent of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin A. If vitamins E and A are to be obtained from no other source, how many grams of the health food must be eaten daily to provide at least the minimum daily requirement of both vitamins? # Answer option: ['A)8.5', 'B)10.5', 'C)12.5', 'D)14.5', 'E)16.5']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how many grams of the health food are required to meet at least 100% of the minimum daily requirement for both vitamin E and vitamin A.

Let's break it down step by step:

1. **Vitamin E Requirement:**
- Each gram of the health food provides 9% of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin E.
- To find out how many grams are needed to meet 100% of the requirement, we set up the equation:
\[
9\% \times \text{grams} = 100\%
\]
- Solving for grams:
\[
\text{grams} = \frac{100\%}{9\%} = \frac{100}{9} \approx 11.11
\]

2. **Vitamin A Requirement:**
- Each gram of the health food provides 8% of the minimum daily requirement of vitamin A.
- To find out how many grams are needed to meet 100% of the requirement, we set up the equation:
\[
8\% \times \text{grams} = 100\%
\]
- Solving for grams:
\[
\text{grams} = \frac{100\%}{8\%} = \frac{100}{8} = 12.5
\]

3. **Determine the Maximum Requirement:**
- To satisfy both vitamin requirements, we need to take the maximum of the two calculated values because we need to meet at least 100% of both vitamins.
- The maximum of 11.11 grams (for vitamin E) and 12.5 grams (for vitamin A) is 12.5 grams.

Therefore, to meet at least the minimum daily requirement for both vitamins, one must consume at least 12.5 grams of the health food.

Final answer: {C}
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: c
Question: A man walks at 5 kmph for 6 hrs and at 4 kmph for 12 hrs. His average speed is # Answer option: ['A)4 1/3 km/h', 'B)7 2/3 km/h', 'C)9 ½ km/h', 'D)8 km/h', 'E)81 km/h']
To find the average speed, we need to calculate the total distance traveled and the total time taken, and then use the formula for average speed:

\[ \text{Average Speed} = \frac{\text{Total Distance}}{\text{Total Time}} \]

**Step 1: Calculate the total distance traveled.**

- For the first part of the journey, the man walks at 5 km/h for 6 hours.
\[
\text{Distance}_1 = \text{Speed} \times \text{Time} = 5 \, \text{km/h} \times 6 \, \text{h} = 30 \, \text{km}
\]

- For the second part of the journey, the man walks at 4 km/h for 12 hours.
\[
\text{Distance}_2 = \text{Speed} \times \text{Time} = 4 \, \text{km/h} \times 12 \, \text{h} = 48 \, \text{km}
\]

- Total distance traveled:
\[
\text{Total Distance} = \text{Distance}_1 + \text{Distance}_2 = 30 \, \text{km} + 48 \, \text{km} = 78 \, \text{km}
\]

**Step 2: Calculate the total time taken.**

- Total time is the sum of the time for both parts of the journey:
\[
\text{Total Time} = 6 \, \text{h} + 12 \, \text{h} = 18 \, \text{h}
\]

**Step 3: Calculate the average speed.**

- Using the formula for average speed:
\[
\text{Average Speed} = \frac{\text{Total Distance}}{\text{Total Time}} = \frac{78 \, \text{km}}{18 \, \text{h}} = 4.3333 \, \text{km/h}
\]

- In fractional form, 4.3333 km/h is equivalent to \(4 \frac{1}{3}\) km/h.

Therefore, the average speed of the man is \(4 \frac{1}{3}\) km/h.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: If a man rows at the rate of 4 kmph in still water and his rate against the current is 2 kmph, then the man's rate along the current is: # Answer option: ['A)15 kmph', 'B)6 kmph', 'C)12 kmph', 'D)14 kmph', 'E)6 kmph']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the man's rate along the current, given his rate in still water and his rate against the current.

Let's define the variables:
- \( v_m \) = man's rate in still water = 4 kmph (from fact1)
- \( v_c \) = rate of the current
- \( v_{against} \) = man's rate against the current = 2 kmph (from fact2)
- \( v_{along} \) = man's rate along the current

We know the following relationships:
1. When rowing against the current, the effective speed is reduced by the speed of the current:
\[
v_{against} = v_m - v_c
\]
Substituting the known values:
\[
2 = 4 - v_c
\]
Solving for \( v_c \):
\[
v_c = 4 - 2 = 2 \text{ kmph}
\]

2. When rowing along the current, the effective speed is increased by the speed of the current:
\[
v_{along} = v_m + v_c
\]
Substituting the known values:
\[
v_{along} = 4 + 2 = 6 \text{ kmph}
\]

Therefore, the man's rate along the current is 6 kmph.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: At what price should the Karan mark a sewing machine that costs him Rs. 1200/- so that even after offering a 20% discount, he makes 20% profit? # Answer option: ['A)1,879', 'B)1,875', 'C)1,876', 'D)1,872', 'E)1,800']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the marked price of the sewing machine such that after offering a 20% discount, Karan still makes a 20% profit on the cost price.

Let's break down the problem step by step:

1. **Determine the Selling Price for 20% Profit:**
- The cost price of the sewing machine is Rs. 1200.
- Karan wants to make a 20% profit on the cost price.
- Profit = 20% of Rs. 1200 = 0.20 * 1200 = Rs. 240.
- Therefore, the selling price (SP) should be Cost Price + Profit = 1200 + 240 = Rs. 1440.

2. **Determine the Marked Price for a 20% Discount:**
- Let the marked price be \( M \).
- Karan offers a 20% discount on the marked price.
- The selling price after the discount is 80% of the marked price (since 100% - 20% = 80%).
- Therefore, 0.80 * M = Rs. 1440.

3. **Solve for the Marked Price:**
- To find the marked price \( M \), we solve the equation:
\[
0.80 \times M = 1440
\]
- Divide both sides by 0.80 to solve for \( M \):
\[
M = \frac{1440}{0.80} = 1800
\]

Thus, the marked price should be Rs. 1800.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: If 27 bottles of soda cost A cents, how much will B bottles cost in dollars?
To determine the cost of B bottles of soda in dollars, given that 27 bottles cost A cents, we can follow these steps:

1. **Find the cost of one bottle in cents:**
- If 27 bottles cost A cents, then the cost of one bottle is \(\frac{A}{27}\) cents.

2. **Find the cost of B bottles in cents:**
- The cost of B bottles would be \(B \times \frac{A}{27}\) cents.

3. **Convert the cost from cents to dollars:**
- Since there are 100 cents in a dollar, the cost in dollars is \(\frac{B \times \frac{A}{27}}{100}\).

4. **Simplify the expression:**
- The expression simplifies to \(\frac{B \times A}{2700}\) dollars.

Therefore, the cost of B bottles in dollars is \(\frac{B \times A}{2700}\).

Final answer: \{\frac{B \times A}{2700}\}

Question: The difference between simple interest and C.I. at the same rate for Rs.5000 for 2 years in Rs.72. The rate of interest is? # Answer option: ['A)10%', 'B)12%', 'C)6%', 'D)8%', 'E)4%']
To solve this problem, we need to find the rate of interest given that the difference between the compound interest (C.I.) and simple interest (S.I.) for Rs. 5000 over 2 years is Rs. 72.

Let's denote:
- Principal (P) = Rs. 5000
- Time (T) = 2 years
- Rate of interest (R) = r%

The formula for simple interest (S.I.) is:
\[ \text{S.I.} = \frac{P \times R \times T}{100} \]

The formula for compound interest (C.I.) is:
\[ \text{C.I.} = P \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^T - P \]

Given that the difference between C.I. and S.I. is Rs. 72, we have:
\[ \text{C.I.} - \text{S.I.} = 72 \]

Substituting the formulas, we get:
\[ P \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - P - \frac{P \times R \times T}{100} = 72 \]

Substitute \( P = 5000 \) and \( T = 2 \):
\[ 5000 \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - 5000 - \frac{5000 \times R \times 2}{100} = 72 \]

Simplify the equation:
\[ 5000 \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - 5000 - 100R = 72 \]

Divide the entire equation by 5000 to simplify:
\[ \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - 1 - \frac{100R}{5000} = \frac{72}{5000} \]

\[ \left(1 + \frac{R}{100}\right)^2 - 1 - \frac{R}{50} = 0.0144 \]

Let \( x = \frac{R}{100} \), then:
\[ (1 + x)^2 - 1 - 2x = 0.0144 \]

Expanding \( (1 + x)^2 \):
\[ 1 + 2x + x^2 - 1 - 2x = 0.0144 \]

This simplifies to:
\[ x^2 = 0.0144 \]

Taking the square root of both sides:
\[ x = \sqrt{0.0144} = 0.12 \]

Since \( x = \frac{R}{100} \), we have:
\[ \frac{R}{100} = 0.12 \]

Thus, \( R = 12\% \).

Therefore, the rate of interest is 12%.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: John conducted a survey about car color. 60% of the people who took the survey were women. Of the men who were surveyed, 75% preferred red cars over green cars. If 10 men liked green cars more than red, how many people took the survey? # Answer option: ['A)100', 'B)120', 'C)50', 'D)200', 'E)80']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the total number of people who took the survey based on the information provided.

1. **Understanding the Facts:**
- Fact 1: 60% of the people who took the survey were women.
- Fact 2: 75% of the men preferred red cars over green cars.
- Fact 3: 10 men liked green cars more than red.

2. **Analyzing Fact 3:**
- If 10 men liked green cars more than red, this means that these 10 men represent the 25% of men who did not prefer red cars (since 75% preferred red).

3. **Calculating the Total Number of Men:**
- If 25% of the men equals 10, then the total number of men can be calculated as follows:
\[
\text{Total number of men} = \frac{10}{0.25} = 40
\]

4. **Calculating the Total Number of People:**
- Since 60% of the people surveyed were women, it follows that 40% were men.
- Let \( x \) be the total number of people surveyed. Then, 40% of \( x \) is equal to the number of men:
\[
0.40x = 40
\]
- Solving for \( x \):
\[
x = \frac{40}{0.40} = 100
\]

5. **Conclusion:**
- The total number of people who took the survey is 100.

Therefore, the final answer is: {A}
Final Answer: a

Question: In a railway station, there are two trains going. One in the harbor line and one in the main line, each having a frequency of 10 minutes. The main line service starts at 5 o'clock and the harbor line starts at 5.02 A.M. A man goes to the station every day to catch the first train that comes. What is the probability of the man catching the first train? # Answer option: ['A)0.9', 'B)0.8', 'C)0.6', 'D)0.65', 'E)1.5']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the probability of the man catching the first train that arrives at the station. We have two trains: one on the main line and one on the harbor line, each with a frequency of 10 minutes.

1. **Main Line Train Schedule:**
- Starts at 5:00 A.M.
- Arrives every 10 minutes: 5:00, 5:10, 5:20, 5:30, etc.

2. **Harbor Line Train Schedule:**
- Starts at 5:02 A.M.
- Arrives every 10 minutes: 5:02, 5:12, 5:22, 5:32, etc.

3. **Time Intervals:**
- Between 5:00 and 5:02, the main line train is the first to arrive.
- Between 5:02 and 5:10, the harbor line train is the first to arrive.
- Between 5:10 and 5:12, the main line train is the first to arrive.
- This pattern repeats every 10 minutes.

4. **Analyzing the Pattern:**
- From 5:00 to 5:10, the main line train is first for 2 minutes (5:00 to 5:02).
- From 5:10 to 5:20, the main line train is first for 2 minutes (5:10 to 5:12).
- This pattern continues, with the main line train being first for 2 out of every 10 minutes.

5. **Probability Calculation:**
- The probability of catching the main line train first is the ratio of the time intervals where the main line train is first to the total time interval.
- Probability = (Time main line is first) / (Total time interval) = 2 minutes / 10 minutes = 0.2

Therefore, the probability of the man catching the first train (main line train) is 0.2.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B? # Answer option: ['A)180', 'B)90', 'C)270', 'D)360', 'E)None of the above']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the distance between points A and B based on the information given.

1. **Understanding the Journey:**
- Kevin drives from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph.
- He then returns from B to A at a constant speed of 90 mph.
- Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was 70 miles away from B.

2. **Analyzing the Information:**
- When Kevin is 70 miles away from B, he is still approaching B. This means he has not yet reached B.
- Since he is traveling at 70 mph towards B, it will take him \( \frac{70 \text{ miles}}{70 \text{ mph}} = 1 \text{ hour} \) to reach B from that point.

3. **Time Calculation:**
- He reaches B 1 hour after being 70 miles away from it.
- The problem states that this moment (when he is 70 miles away from B) is exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip.
- Therefore, after reaching B, he has 2 hours left to complete his trip back to A.

4. **Return Journey:**
- Kevin returns from B to A at 90 mph.
- Since he has 2 hours to complete the return journey, the distance from B to A is \( 90 \text{ mph} \times 2 \text{ hours} = 180 \text{ miles} \).

5. **Distance from A to B:**
- The distance from A to B is the same as the distance from B to A, which is 180 miles.

Thus, the distance between A and B is 180 miles.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: The telephone bill of a certain establishment is partly fixed and partly varies as the number of calls consumed. When in a certain month 540 calls made the bill is Rs.1800. In another month 620 calls are consumed then the bill becomes Rs.2040. In another month 500 units are consumed due to more holidays. The bill for that month would be: # Answer option: ['A)Rs.1560', 'B)Rs.1680', 'C)Rs.1840', 'D)Rs.1950', 'E)Rs.1690']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the fixed and variable components of the telephone bill.

Let's denote:
- \( F \) as the fixed part of the bill.
- \( V \) as the variable cost per call.

From the given information:
1. When 540 calls are made, the bill is Rs.1800.
\[
F + 540V = 1800
\]
2. When 620 calls are made, the bill is Rs.2040.
\[
F + 620V = 2040
\]

We have two equations:
1. \( F + 540V = 1800 \)
2. \( F + 620V = 2040 \)

To find \( V \), we subtract the first equation from the second:
\[
(F + 620V) - (F + 540V) = 2040 - 1800
\]
\[
620V - 540V = 240
\]
\[
80V = 240
\]
\[
V = \frac{240}{80} = 3
\]

Now that we have \( V = 3 \), we can substitute back into one of the original equations to find \( F \). Using the first equation:
\[
F + 540 \times 3 = 1800
\]
\[
F + 1620 = 1800
\]
\[
F = 1800 - 1620 = 180
\]

Now we have:
- Fixed cost \( F = 180 \)
- Variable cost per call \( V = 3 \)

For a month with 500 calls, the bill would be:
\[
\text{Bill} = F + 500V = 180 + 500 \times 3
\]
\[
\text{Bill} = 180 + 1500 = 1680
\]

Thus, the bill for the month with 500 calls is Rs.1680.

Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another? # Answer option: ['A)1 hr 23 min', 'B)1 hr 15 min', 'C)1 hr 8 min', 'D)56 min', 'E)55 min']
To determine when the two trains cross each other, we need to calculate the time it takes for them to meet after the first train departs.

1. **Train M's Journey:**
- Train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9 am.
- Total travel time for Train M = 4 hours.

2. **Train N's Journey:**
- Train N leaves City B at 7 am and reaches City A at 10:30 am.
- Total travel time for Train N = 3.5 hours.

3. **Relative Speed and Meeting Point:**
- Both trains are traveling towards each other.
- Train M travels for 2 hours before Train N starts (from 5 am to 7 am).
- In these 2 hours, Train M covers half of its journey (since it takes 4 hours in total), meaning it has covered half the distance between City A and City B.

4. **Remaining Distance:**
- At 7 am, Train M has covered half the distance, and Train N starts its journey.
- The remaining distance is half the total distance between City A and City B.

5. **Time to Meet:**
- Train M and Train N are now moving towards each other.
- Train M has 2 hours left to reach City B, and Train N has 3.5 hours to reach City A.
- The combined speed of both trains will cover the remaining half distance.

6. **Calculating the Meeting Time:**
- Since Train M covers the entire distance in 4 hours, it covers half the distance in 2 hours.
- Train N covers the entire distance in 3.5 hours, so it covers half the distance in 1.75 hours.
- The time taken for both trains to meet is the time taken to cover the remaining half distance when both are moving towards each other.

7. **Relative Speed Calculation:**
- Let the total distance be D.
- Train M's speed = D/4 per hour.
- Train N's speed = D/3.5 per hour.
- Combined speed = (D/4 + D/3.5) per hour = (7D/28 + 4D/14) = (7D + 8D)/28 = 15D/28 per hour.

8. **Time to Cross:**
- Time taken to cover half the distance (D/2) = (D/2) / (15D/28) = (D/2) * (28/15D) = 28/30 = 14/15 hours.

9. **Convert to Minutes:**
- 14/15 hours = 14/15 * 60 minutes = 56 minutes.

Therefore, the two trains cross each other 56 minutes after Train N starts its journey at 7 am, which is at 7:56 am.

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: If Q, a positive integer, has 5 factors, which of the following must be true about Q? I. Q is the square of a prime number. II. Q is the fourth power of a prime number. III. Q is the product of two prime numbers. # Answer option: ['A)I only', 'B)III only', 'C)II only', 'D)I and II only', 'E)I and III only']
To determine which statements about \( Q \) must be true, we need to analyze the condition that \( Q \) has exactly 5 factors.

1. **Understanding the number of factors:**
- If \( Q \) is a positive integer with a prime factorization of \( Q = p_1^{a_1} \times p_2^{a_2} \times \ldots \times p_n^{a_n} \), the number of factors of \( Q \) is given by \( (a_1 + 1)(a_2 + 1) \ldots (a_n + 1) \).
- We need this product to equal 5.

2. **Analyzing the possibilities:**
- Since 5 is a prime number, the only way to express 5 as a product of integers is \( 5 = 5 \times 1 \).
- This implies that one of the exponents \( a_i \) must be 4, and all other exponents must be 0. Therefore, \( Q \) must be of the form \( p^4 \), where \( p \) is a prime number.

3. **Evaluating the statements:**
- **Statement I:** \( Q \) is the square of a prime number.
- If \( Q = p^2 \), the number of factors would be \( (2 + 1) = 3 \), not 5. Therefore, this statement is false.
- **Statement II:** \( Q \) is the fourth power of a prime number.
- If \( Q = p^4 \), the number of factors is \( (4 + 1) = 5 \). This statement is true.
- **Statement III:** \( Q \) is the product of two prime numbers.
- If \( Q = p_1 \times p_2 \), where \( p_1 \) and \( p_2 \) are distinct primes, the number of factors would be \( (1 + 1)(1 + 1) = 4 \), not 5. Therefore, this statement is false.

4. **Conclusion:**
- Only Statement II is true based on the analysis.

Final answer: {C}
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: b

How long does it take Jill to finish the remaining work? # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)8', 'C)22', 'D)50', 'E)20']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how long it takes Jill to finish the remaining work after Jack has completed two-thirds of it.

1. **Determine Jack's rate of work:**
- Jack can clean the entire yacht in 12 hours. Therefore, his rate of work is \( \frac{1}{12} \) of the yacht per hour.

2. **Calculate the work Jack has completed:**
- Jack finishes two-thirds of the work. Therefore, the work he has completed is \( \frac{2}{3} \) of the yacht.

3. **Calculate the remaining work:**
- The remaining work is \( 1 - \frac{2}{3} = \frac{1}{3} \) of the yacht.

4. **Determine Jill's rate of work:**
- Jill's rate of cleaning is 5% of Jack's rate. Therefore, Jill's rate is \( 0.05 \times \frac{1}{12} = \frac{1}{240} \) of the yacht per hour.

5. **Calculate the time it takes Jill to finish the remaining work:**
- Jill needs to complete \( \frac{1}{3} \) of the yacht. Since her rate is \( \frac{1}{240} \) of the yacht per hour, the time \( t \) it takes her to complete the remaining work is given by:
\[
t = \frac{\text{Remaining work}}{\text{Jill's rate}} = \frac{\frac{1}{3}}{\frac{1}{240}} = \frac{1}{3} \times 240 = 80 \text{ hours}
\]

Question: Train A leaves a station every 16 minutes and Train B leaves every 17 minutes. If both trains just left the station simultaneously, how long until they do so again? # Answer option: ['A)272 minutes', 'B)304 minutes', 'C)190 minutes', 'D)70 minutes', 'E)35 minutes']
To determine when both trains will leave the station simultaneously again, we need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of the two departure intervals: 16 minutes for Train A and 17 minutes for Train B.

1. **Identify the numbers**: We have 16 and 17.

2. **Prime factorization**:
- 16 is \(2^4\).
- 17 is a prime number, so its prime factorization is \(17^1\).

3. **Calculate the LCM**:
- The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime number that appears in the factorizations.
- For 2, the highest power is \(2^4\).
- For 17, the highest power is \(17^1\).

4. **Multiply these together**:
\[
\text{LCM} = 2^4 \times 17^1 = 16 \times 17
\]

5. **Calculate the product**:
\[
16 \times 17 = 272
\]

Thus, the least common multiple of 16 and 17 is 272 minutes. This means both trains will leave the station simultaneously again after 272 minutes.

Final answer: {A}

To solve this problem, we need to determine what percentage the astronaut's weight on Venus is of their weight on Earth.

1. **Identify the weights:**
- Weight on Earth = 211 pounds
- Weight on Venus = 182 pounds

2. **Calculate the percentage:**
- The formula to find the percentage is: \(\text{Percentage} = \left(\frac{\text{Weight on Venus}}{\text{Weight on Earth}}\right) \times 100\)

3. **Substitute the given values:**
\[
\text{Percentage} = \left(\frac{182}{211}\right) \times 100
\]

\[
\frac{182}{211} \approx 0.8626
\]

5. **Convert to percentage:**
\[
0.8626 \times 100 \approx 86.26\%
\]

6. **Round to the nearest whole number:**
- 86.26% rounds to 86%.

Question: A starts travel towards south 3km, then travel 5 km towards east, and again travels 3 km to north, and finally travels 2km towards west. In the end how far from is A from home? # Answer option: ['A)3km', 'B)2km', 'C)4km', 'D)5km', 'E)6km']
To determine how far A is from the starting point, we need to analyze each segment of the journey and calculate the net displacement.

1. **Initial Position:** A starts at the origin (0, 0).

2. **First Movement:** A travels 3 km south.
- This moves A to (0, -3).

3. **Second Movement:** A travels 5 km east.
- This moves A to (5, -3).

4. **Third Movement:** A travels 3 km north.
- This moves A to (5, 0).

5. **Fourth Movement:** A travels 2 km west.
- This moves A to (3, 0).

Now, we calculate the distance from the final position (3, 0) back to the origin (0, 0). The distance is the straight-line distance, which is simply the x-coordinate difference since the y-coordinate is 0.

- Distance = |3 - 0| = 3 km

Therefore, A is 3 km away from the starting point.

Question: A rectangle has a length of 8 centimeters and a width of 3 centimeters. Find the perimeter. # Answer option: ['A)18cm', 'B)22cm', 'C)20cm', 'D)30cm', 'E)28cm']
To find the perimeter of a rectangle, we use the formula:

\[ \text{Perimeter} = 2 \times (\text{Length} + \text{Width}) \]

Given:
- Length = 8 centimeters
- Width = 3 centimeters

Substitute these values into the formula:

\[ \text{Perimeter} = 2 \times (8 + 3) \]

Calculate the sum inside the parentheses:

\[ 8 + 3 = 11 \]

Now, multiply by 2:

\[ 2 \times 11 = 22 \]

Therefore, the perimeter of the rectangle is 22 centimeters.

Question: If m > 0, y > 0, and x is m percent of 4y, then, in terms of y, m is what percentage of x? # Answer option: ['A)y/400', 'B)4y', 'C)50y', 'D)2500/y', 'E)5000/y']
To solve this problem, we need to express \( m \) as a percentage of \( x \) in terms of \( y \).

Given:
1. \( m > 0 \)
2. \( y > 0 \)
3. \( x \) is \( m \) percent of \( 4y \).

From fact 3, we can express \( x \) in terms of \( m \) and \( y \):
\[ x = \frac{m}{100} \times 4y \]
\[ x = \frac{4my}{100} \]
\[ x = \frac{4my}{100} = \frac{my}{25} \]

Now, we need to find what percentage \( m \) is of \( x \). This means we need to find the ratio of \( m \) to \( x \) and then convert it to a percentage.

The ratio of \( m \) to \( x \) is:
\[ \frac{m}{x} = \frac{m}{\frac{my}{25}} \]

Simplifying the expression:
\[ \frac{m}{x} = \frac{m \times 25}{my} \]
\[ \frac{m}{x} = \frac{25}{y} \]

To convert this ratio into a percentage, we multiply by 100:
\[ \left(\frac{m}{x}\right) \times 100 = \frac{25}{y} \times 100 \]
\[ = \frac{2500}{y} \]

Thus, \( m \) is \(\frac{2500}{y}\) percent of \( x \).

Question: Suppose for any real number x, [x] denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to x. Let L(x,y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] and R(x,y) = [2x] + [2y]. Then it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers x and y for which # Answer option: ['A)L(x,y) = R(x,y)', 'B)L(x,y) ≠ R(x,y)', 'C)L(x,y) < R(x,y)', 'D)L(x,y) < R(x,y)', 'E)None']
To solve this problem, we need to analyze the expressions \( L(x, y) \) and \( R(x, y) \) and determine the relationship between them for positive real numbers \( x \) and \( y \).

### Step 1: Analyze \( L(x, y) \)

Given:
\[ L(x, y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y] \]

- \([x]\) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( x \).
- \([y]\) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( y \).
- \([x + y]\) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( x + y \).

### Step 2: Analyze \( R(x, y) \)

Given:
\[ R(x, y) = [2x] + [2y] \]

- \([2x]\) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( 2x \).
- \([2y]\) is the greatest integer less than or equal to \( 2y \).

### Step 3: Compare \( L(x, y) \) and \( R(x, y) \)

To compare \( L(x, y) \) and \( R(x, y) \), consider the following:

- The expression \([x + y]\) can be either \([x] + [y]\) or \([x] + [y] + 1\), depending on whether the fractional parts of \( x \) and \( y \) sum to 1 or more.
- The expression \([2x]\) is \( 2[x] \) or \( 2[x] + 1\) depending on whether the fractional part of \( x \) is less than 0.5 or not.
- Similarly, \([2y]\) is \( 2[y] \) or \( 2[y] + 1\) depending on whether the fractional part of \( y \) is less than 0.5 or not.

### Step 4: Consider Specific Cases

1. **Case 1: \( x = 0.5, y = 0.5 \)**
- \([x] = 0\), \([y] = 0\), \([x + y] = 1\)
- \( L(x, y) = 0 + 0 + 1 = 1 \)
- \([2x] = 1\), \([2y] = 1\)
- \( R(x, y) = 1 + 1 = 2 \)
- Here, \( L(x, y) \neq R(x, y) \).

2. **Case 2: \( x = 0.25, y = 0.25 \)**
- \([x] = 0\), \([y] = 0\), \([x + y] = 0\)
- \( L(x, y) = 0 + 0 + 0 = 0 \)
- \([2x] = 0\), \([2y] = 0\)
- \( R(x, y) = 0 + 0 = 0 \)
- Here, \( L(x, y) = R(x, y) \).

### Conclusion

From the cases above, we see that it is possible for \( L(x, y) = R(x, y) \) and also for \( L(x, y) \neq R(x, y) \). Therefore, it is not impossible to find two positive real numbers \( x \) and \( y \) such that \( L(x, y) = R(x, y) \).

Thus, the correct answer is that it is impossible to find any two positive real numbers \( x \) and \( y \) for which \( L(x, y) \neq R(x, y) \) is not true, as we have found such examples.

Question: On a normal day Bill usually averages about 15 mph when riding his bicycle. On a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph. How far can Bill travel on a windy day in 21 minutes? Round to the nearest hundredth.
To determine how far Bill can travel on a windy day in 21 minutes, we need to follow these steps:

1. **Determine Bill's speed on a windy day:**
- According to fact 1, Bill usually averages about 15 mph.
- According to fact 2, on a windy day, his speed is reduced by 4 mph.
- Therefore, on a windy day, Bill's speed is \(15 \text{ mph} - 4 \text{ mph} = 11 \text{ mph}\).

2. **Convert the time from minutes to hours:**
- There are 60 minutes in an hour.
- Bill is traveling for 21 minutes.
- To convert minutes to hours, divide the number of minutes by 60:
\[
\text{Time in hours} = \frac{21}{60} = 0.35 \text{ hours}
\]

3. **Calculate the distance traveled:**
- Distance is calculated using the formula: \(\text{Distance} = \text{Speed} \times \text{Time}\).
- Bill's speed on a windy day is 11 mph, and the time is 0.35 hours.
- Therefore, the distance Bill can travel is:
\[
\text{Distance} = 11 \text{ mph} \times 0.35 \text{ hours} = 3.85 \text{ miles}
\]

4. **Round the distance to the nearest hundredth:**
- The calculated distance is already at two decimal places: 3.85 miles.

Thus, the final answer is: \(\text{Final answer:} \{3.85\}\)

Question: At an election meeting 10 speakers are to address the meeting. The only protocol to be observed is that whenever they speak the pm should speak before the mp and the mp should speak before the mla. In how many ways can the meeting be held? # Answer option: ['A)10!/3', 'B)10!/6', 'C)10!/2', 'D)10!/4', 'E)10!/5']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of ways to arrange 10 speakers such that the protocol is followed. The protocol states that the pm should speak before the mp, and the mp should speak before the mla.

Let's assume that among the 10 speakers, there is exactly one pm, one mp, and one mla. The remaining 7 speakers can be any other individuals.

1. **Total Arrangements Without Restrictions:**
- If there were no restrictions, the 10 speakers could be arranged in \(10!\) ways.

2. **Applying the Protocol:**
- According to the protocol, the pm must speak before the mp, and the mp must speak before the mla. This means that for any arrangement of these three specific speakers, there is only 1 valid order (pm, mp, mla).
- Without any restrictions, these 3 speakers can be arranged among themselves in \(3!\) ways.

3. **Calculating Valid Arrangements:**
- Since only 1 of the \(3!\) arrangements of pm, mp, and mla is valid, we need to divide the total number of unrestricted arrangements by the number of invalid arrangements.
- Therefore, the number of valid arrangements is \(\frac{10!}{3!}\).

4. **Simplifying the Calculation:**
- Calculate \(3! = 3 \times 2 \times 1 = 6\).
- Thus, the number of valid arrangements is \(\frac{10!}{6}\).

5. **Final Answer:**
- The correct answer is option B, which corresponds to \(\frac{10!}{6}\).

To solve this problem, we need to determine how many minutes it will take for \( y \) gallons to pass through the drain at the given rate.

1. **Understand the rate of flow:**
The liquid passes through the drain at a rate of \( \frac{w}{25} \) gallons every \( x \) seconds. This means in \( x \) seconds, \( \frac{w}{25} \) gallons pass through.

2. **Convert the rate to gallons per second:**
To find the rate in gallons per second, we divide the amount of liquid by the time in seconds:
\[
\text{Rate in gallons per second} = \frac{\frac{w}{25}}{x} = \frac{w}{25x}
\]

3. **Determine the time in seconds to pass \( y \) gallons:**
To find out how many seconds it takes for \( y \) gallons to pass through, we set up the equation:
\[
\text{Time in seconds} = \frac{y}{\text{Rate in gallons per second}} = \frac{y}{\frac{w}{25x}} = \frac{25xy}{w}
\]

4. **Convert the time from seconds to minutes:**
Since there are 60 seconds in a minute, we convert the time from seconds to minutes by dividing by 60:
\[
\text{Time in minutes} = \frac{25xy}{w} \times \frac{1}{60} = \frac{25xy}{60w} = \frac{5xy}{12w}
\]

5. **Select the correct answer:**

Question: Amy is organizing her bookshelves and finds that she has 10 different types of books. She then codes each book with either a single letter or a pair of two different letters. If each type of book is uniquely represented by either a single letter or pair of letters, what is the smallest number of letters Amy will need to create the codes for all 10 types of books? (Assume the order of letters in a pair does not matter.) # Answer option: ['A)3', 'B)4', 'C)5', 'D)10', 'E)20']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the smallest number of letters required to create unique codes for 10 different types of books, using either a single letter or a pair of two different letters. The order of letters in a pair does not matter, which means pairs like "AB" and "BA" are considered the same.

Let's break down the problem:

1. **Single Letter Codes**: If we use \( n \) different letters, we can create \( n \) unique single-letter codes.

2. **Pair of Letters Codes**: For pairs of letters, since the order does not matter, the number of unique pairs we can form from \( n \) letters is given by the combination formula \( \binom{n}{2} = \frac{n(n-1)}{2} \).

3. **Total Codes**: The total number of unique codes we can create using \( n \) letters is the sum of single-letter codes and pair-of-letters codes:
\[
\text{Total Codes} = n + \binom{n}{2} = n + \frac{n(n-1)}{2}
\]

We need this total to be at least 10, as there are 10 different types of books.

Let's calculate this for different values of \( n \):

- **For \( n = 3 \):**
\[
\text{Total Codes} = 3 + \binom{3}{2} = 3 + 3 = 6
\]
This is not enough.

- **For \( n = 4 \):**
\[
\text{Total Codes} = 4 + \binom{4}{2} = 4 + 6 = 10
\]
This is exactly 10, which is sufficient.

- **For \( n = 5 \):**
\[
\text{Total Codes} = 5 + \binom{5}{2} = 5 + 10 = 15
\]
This is more than enough, but we are looking for the smallest \( n \).

Since \( n = 4 \) gives us exactly 10 codes, which is the minimum required, the smallest number of letters needed is 4.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: For bringing each copper coin from the bottom of a river, a coin-diver gets 20 cents, and for each brass coin she gets 25 cents. If after one dive, she got $3.40. What is the minimum number of copper coins that she brought? # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)3', 'C)2', 'D)1', 'E)0']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the minimum number of copper coins the diver could have brought up, given that she earned a total of $3.40 from a combination of copper and brass coins.

1. **Convert the total earnings to cents**:
$3.40 is equivalent to 340 cents.

2. **Define variables**:
Let \( x \) be the number of copper coins and \( y \) be the number of brass coins.

3. **Set up the equation based on earnings**:
Each copper coin earns 20 cents, and each brass coin earns 25 cents. Therefore, the equation for the total earnings is:
\[
20x + 25y = 340
\]

4. **Simplify the equation**:
To simplify, divide the entire equation by 5:
\[
4x + 5y = 68
\]

5. **Find integer solutions**:
We need to find non-negative integer solutions for \( x \) and \( y \) that satisfy this equation. We are particularly interested in minimizing \( x \).

6. **Test values for \( y \) to find the minimum \( x \)**:
- If \( y = 0 \):
\[
4x = 68 \implies x = 17
\]
- If \( y = 1 \):
\[
4x + 5 = 68 \implies 4x = 63 \implies x = 15.75 \quad (\text{not an integer})
\]
- If \( y = 2 \):
\[
4x + 10 = 68 \implies 4x = 58 \implies x = 14.5 \quad (\text{not an integer})
\]
- If \( y = 3 \):
\[
4x + 15 = 68 \implies 4x = 53 \implies x = 13.25 \quad (\text{not an integer})
\]
- If \( y = 4 \):
\[
4x + 20 = 68 \implies 4x = 48 \implies x = 12
\]
- If \( y = 5 \):
\[
4x + 25 = 68 \implies 4x = 43 \implies x = 10.75 \quad (\text{not an integer})
\]
- If \( y = 6 \):
\[
4x + 30 = 68 \implies 4x = 38 \implies x = 9.5 \quad (\text{not an integer})
\]
- If \( y = 7 \):
\[
4x + 35 = 68 \implies 4x = 33 \implies x = 8.25 \quad (\text{not an integer})
\]
- If \( y = 8 \):
\[
4x + 40 = 68 \implies 4x = 28 \implies x = 7
\]
- If \( y = 9 \):
\[
4x + 45 = 68 \implies 4x = 23 \implies x = 5.75 \quad (\text{not an integer})
\]
- If \( y = 10 \):
\[
4x + 50 = 68 \implies 4x = 18 \implies x = 4.5 \quad (\text{not an integer})
\]
- If \( y = 11 \):
\[
4x + 55 = 68 \implies 4x = 13 \implies x = 3.25 \quad (\text{not an integer})
\]
- If \( y = 12 \):
\[
4x + 60 = 68 \implies 4x = 8 \implies x = 2
\]

7. **Conclusion**:
The minimum integer value for \( x \) is 2 when \( y = 12 \).

Therefore, the minimum number of copper coins she brought is 2.

\[

\]

0.0005 \times x = 8

\[
x = \frac{8}{0.0005}

\]

\[

\]

Question: What is the largest integral value of 'k' for which the quadratic equation x2 - 5x + k = 0 will have two real and distinct roots? # Answer option: ['A)9', 'B)7', 'C)3', 'D)8', 'E)12']
To determine the largest integral value of \( k \) for which the quadratic equation \( x^2 - 5x + k = 0 \) has two real and distinct roots, we need to use the discriminant condition for real and distinct roots.

The discriminant \(\Delta\) of a quadratic equation \( ax^2 + bx + c = 0 \) is given by:

\[
\Delta = b^2 - 4ac
\]

For the quadratic equation to have two real and distinct roots, the discriminant must be greater than zero:

\[
\Delta > 0
\]

In our equation, \( a = 1 \), \( b = -5 \), and \( c = k \). Plugging these values into the discriminant formula gives:

\[
\Delta = (-5)^2 - 4 \cdot 1 \cdot k = 25 - 4k
\]

We need:

\[
25 - 4k > 0
\]

Solving this inequality:

\[
25 > 4k
\]

\[
\frac{25}{4} > k
\]

\[
k < 6.25
\]

Since \( k \) must be an integer, the largest integer less than 6.25 is 6. Therefore, the largest integral value of \( k \) for which the quadratic equation has two real and distinct roots is 6.

However, the answer options provided are ['A)9', 'B)7', 'C)3', 'D)8', 'E)12']. The closest option to 6 is 7, but 7 is not less than 6.25. Therefore, the correct answer based on the options provided is not directly available.

Re-evaluating the options, the largest possible value of \( k \) that satisfies \( k < 6.25 \) is 6, but since 6 is not an option, we must choose the next logical option that fits the context of the problem, which is 3, as it is the only option less than 6.25.

Final answer: {C}
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: c
Question: The height of a room to its semi-perimeter is 2:5. It costs Rs.260 to paper the walls of the room with paper 50cm wide at Rs.2 per meter allowing an area of 15 sq.m for doors and windows. The height of the room is: # Answer option: ['A)2.6m', 'B)3.9m', 'C)4m', 'D)4.2m', 'E)4.4m']
To solve this problem, we need to find the height of the room given the ratio of the height to the semi-perimeter and the cost of papering the walls.

1. **Understanding the Ratio:**
- The ratio of the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is given as 2:5. Let's denote the height of the room as \( h \) and the semi-perimeter as \( s \).
- Therefore, \( \frac{h}{s} = \frac{2}{5} \) or \( h = \frac{2}{5} \times s \).

2. **Cost of Papering the Walls:**
- The cost to paper the walls is Rs. 260.
- The paper is 50 cm wide, which is 0.5 meters wide, and costs Rs. 2 per meter.
- Therefore, the cost per square meter of paper is \( \frac{2}{0.5} = 4 \) Rs/m².

3. **Calculating the Area to be Papered:**
- The total cost is Rs. 260, and the cost per square meter is Rs. 4.
- Therefore, the total area to be papered is \( \frac{260}{4} = 65 \) m².
- However, we need to allow an area of 15 m² for doors and windows, so the actual area of the walls is \( 65 + 15 = 80 \) m².

4. **Relating the Area to the Room Dimensions:**
- The area of the walls of the room is given by the formula: \( \text{Area} = \text{Perimeter} \times \text{Height} \).
- Let the perimeter of the room be \( P \). Then, \( \text{Area} = P \times h = 80 \) m².
- The semi-perimeter \( s = \frac{P}{2} \).

5. **Substituting the Ratio:**
- From the ratio, \( h = \frac{2}{5} \times s \).
- Therefore, \( P = 2s \) and substituting \( h = \frac{2}{5} \times s \) into the area equation:
\[
P \times h = 80 \implies 2s \times \frac{2}{5} \times s = 80
\]
\[
\frac{4}{5} s^2 = 80
\]
\[
s^2 = 80 \times \frac{5}{4} = 100
\]
\[
s = 10
\]

6. **Finding the Height:**
- Now, substitute \( s = 10 \) back into the height equation:
\[
h = \frac{2}{5} \times 10 = 4
\]

Therefore, the height of the room is 4 meters.

Final answer: {C}
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: c
Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find that number. # Answer option: ['A)1584', 'B)2520', 'C)1728', 'D)1656', 'E)None']
To solve this problem, we need to find the number such that the difference between \(\frac{7}{8}\) of the number and \(\frac{7}{18}\) of the number is 770.

Let's denote the number as \( x \).

1. **Calculate \(\frac{7}{8}\) of the number:**
\[
\frac{7}{8} \times x = \frac{7x}{8}
\]

2. **Calculate \(\frac{7}{18}\) of the number:**
\[
\frac{7}{18} \times x = \frac{7x}{18}
\]

3. **Set up the equation for the difference:**
\[
\frac{7x}{8} - \frac{7x}{18} = 770
\]

4. **Find a common denominator to combine the fractions:**
The least common multiple of 8 and 18 is 72.

Convert each fraction:
\[
\frac{7x}{8} = \frac{7x \times 9}{72} = \frac{63x}{72}
\]
\[
\frac{7x}{18} = \frac{7x \times 4}{72} = \frac{28x}{72}
\]

5. **Subtract the fractions:**
\[
\frac{63x}{72} - \frac{28x}{72} = \frac{35x}{72}
\]

6. **Set the equation equal to 770:**
\[
\frac{35x}{72} = 770
\]

7. **Solve for \( x \):**
Multiply both sides by 72 to clear the fraction:
\[
35x = 770 \times 72
\]

Calculate \( 770 \times 72 \):
\[
770 \times 72 = 55440
\]

Divide both sides by 35:
\[
x = \frac{55440}{35}
\]

Calculate \( \frac{55440}{35} \):
\[
x = 1584
\]

Thus, the number is 1584. Therefore, the final answer is:

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: Boomtown urban planners expect the city’s population to increase by 10% per year over the next two years. If that projection were to come true, the population two years from now would be exactly double the population of one year ago. Which of the following is closest to the percent population increase in Boomtown over the last year? # Answer option: ['A)20%', 'B)40%', 'C)50%', 'D)65%', 'E)75%']
To solve this problem, we need to analyze the given facts and determine the percent population increase over the last year.

Let's denote the population one year ago as \( P \).

According to fact 1, the population is expected to increase by 10% per year over the next two years. Therefore, the population at the end of the first year will be:
\[ P \times 1.10 \]

At the end of the second year, the population will be:
\[ P \times 1.10 \times 1.10 = P \times 1.21 \]

According to fact 2, the population two years from now will be exactly double the population of one year ago. Therefore, we have:
\[ P \times 1.21 = 2 \times P_{\text{one year ago}} \]

\[ P_{\text{one year ago}} = P \times (1 + x) \]

Question: A retailer sold an appliance for 40 percent above cost, which represented a gross profit of $20.00. For what price did the retailer sell the appliance? # Answer option: ['A)$27.30', 'B)$51.00', 'C)$63.00', 'D)$70.00', 'E)$91.00']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the selling price of the appliance based on the given facts.

1. **Understanding the Facts:**
- Fact 1: The appliance was sold for 40 percent above cost.
- Fact 2: The gross profit from the sale was $20.00.

2. **Setting Up the Equation:**
- Let \( C \) be the cost price of the appliance.
- The selling price is 40% above the cost price, which can be expressed as:
\[
\text{Selling Price} = C + 0.4C = 1.4C
\]
- The gross profit is the difference between the selling price and the cost price:
\[
\text{Gross Profit} = \text{Selling Price} - C = 1.4C - C = 0.4C
\]
- We know from Fact 2 that the gross profit is $20.00:
\[
0.4C = 20
\]

3. **Solving for the Cost Price:**
- Solve the equation for \( C \):
\[
C = \frac{20}{0.4} = 50
\]
- So, the cost price of the appliance is $50.00.

4. **Calculating the Selling Price:**
- Substitute \( C = 50 \) into the equation for the selling price:
\[
\text{Selling Price} = 1.4 \times 50 = 70
\]

5. **Conclusion:**
- The retailer sold the appliance for $70.00.

Therefore, the correct answer is option D.

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: An express electric train takes exact three seconds to enter tunnel which is 1 mile long. If train is traveling at 120 mile an hour, how long will it take to pass completely through the tunnel? # Answer option: ['A)43 seconds', 'B)39 seconds', 'C)20 seconds', 'D)33 seconds', 'E)55 seconds']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how long it takes for the entire train to pass completely through the tunnel.

1. **Determine the length of the train:**
- The train takes 3 seconds to enter the tunnel. During this time, the entire length of the train enters the tunnel.
- The speed of the train is 120 miles per hour. We need to convert this speed into miles per second to find out how far the train travels in 3 seconds.
- There are 3600 seconds in an hour, so the speed of the train in miles per second is:
\[
\frac{120 \text{ miles/hour}}{3600 \text{ seconds/hour}} = \frac{1}{30} \text{ miles/second}
\]
- In 3 seconds, the train travels:
\[
3 \times \frac{1}{30} = \frac{3}{30} = \frac{1}{10} \text{ miles}
\]
- Therefore, the length of the train is \(\frac{1}{10}\) miles.

2. **Determine the total distance to be covered:**
- The train needs to pass completely through the tunnel, which means it needs to cover the length of the tunnel plus its own length.
- The tunnel is 1 mile long, and the train is \(\frac{1}{10}\) miles long.
- Total distance to be covered is:
\[
1 + \frac{1}{10} = \frac{10}{10} + \frac{1}{10} = \frac{11}{10} \text{ miles}
\]

3. **Calculate the time to pass through the tunnel:**
- We already know the speed of the train is \(\frac{1}{30}\) miles per second.
- Time taken to cover \(\frac{11}{10}\) miles is:
\[
\frac{\frac{11}{10} \text{ miles}}{\frac{1}{30} \text{ miles/second}} = \frac{11}{10} \times 30 = 33 \text{ seconds}
\]

Therefore, the train will take 33 seconds to pass completely through the tunnel.

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: An exam is given in a certain class. The average (arithmetic mean) of the highest score and the lowest score is equal to x. If the average score for the entire class is equal to y and there are z students in the class, where z > 5, then in terms of x, y, and z, what is the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers? # Answer option: ['A)(zy – 2x)/z', 'B)(zy – 2)/z', 'C)(zx – y)/(z – 2)', 'D)(zy – 2x)/(z -2)', 'E)(zy – x)/(z + 2)']
To solve this problem, we need to find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers. Let's break down the information given and the steps needed to find the solution:

1. **Understand the given facts:**
- Fact 1: The average of the highest score (H) and the lowest score (L) is equal to x. This can be expressed as:
\[
\frac{H + L}{2} = x \implies H + L = 2x
\]

- Fact 2: The average score for the entire class is y. If there are z students, the total sum of all scores (S) is:
\[
\frac{S}{z} = y \implies S = zy
\]

- Fact 3: There are z students in the class, where z > 5.

2. **Find the sum of scores excluding the highest and lowest scores:**
- The total sum of all scores is S = zy.
- The sum of the highest and lowest scores is H + L = 2x.
- Therefore, the sum of the scores excluding the highest and lowest scores is:
\[
S - (H + L) = zy - 2x
\]

3. **Calculate the number of students excluding the highest and lowest scorers:**
- There are z students in total.
- Excluding the highest and lowest scorers, there are z - 2 students.

4. **Find the average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers:**
- The average score for the class excluding the highest and lowest scorers is the sum of the scores excluding the highest and lowest scores divided by the number of students excluding the highest and lowest scorers:
\[
\text{Average} = \frac{zy - 2x}{z - 2}
\]

5. **Match the expression to the answer options:**
- The expression we derived is \(\frac{zy - 2x}{z - 2}\), which matches option D.

Therefore, the final answer is: \(\text{Final answer:}\{D\}\)
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: Jerry purchased a 1-year $5,000 bond that paid an annual interest rate of 12% compounded every six months. How much interest had this bond accrued at maturity?
To determine the interest accrued on Jerry's bond at maturity, we need to calculate the compound interest using the given information. Let's break it down step by step:

1. **Identify the Principal Amount (P):**
The principal amount of the bond is $5,000.

2. **Determine the Annual Interest Rate (r):**
The annual interest rate is 12%.

3. **Identify the Compounding Frequency:**
The interest is compounded every six months, which means it is compounded semi-annually. Therefore, the number of compounding periods per year (n) is 2.

4. **Calculate the Interest Rate per Compounding Period:**
Since the interest is compounded semi-annually, we divide the annual interest rate by the number of compounding periods per year:
\[
\text{Interest rate per period} = \frac{12\%}{2} = 6\% = 0.06
\]

5. **Determine the Total Number of Compounding Periods (t):**
The bond is for 1 year, and since it compounds semi-annually, there are 2 compounding periods in total.

6. **Use the Compound Interest Formula:**
The formula for compound interest is:
\[
A = P \left(1 + \frac{r}{n}\right)^{nt}
\]
where:
- \( A \) is the amount of money accumulated after n years, including interest.
- \( P \) is the principal amount ($5,000).
- \( r \) is the annual interest rate (0.12).
- \( n \) is the number of times that interest is compounded per year (2).
- \( t \) is the time the money is invested for in years (1).

Plugging in the values:
\[
A = 5000 \left(1 + \frac{0.12}{2}\right)^{2 \times 1}
\]
\[
A = 5000 \left(1 + 0.06\right)^{2}
\]
\[
A = 5000 \times (1.06)^2
\]
\[
A = 5000 \times 1.1236
\]
\[
A = 5618
\]

7. **Calculate the Interest Accrued:**
The interest accrued is the total amount minus the principal:
\[
\text{Interest} = A - P = 5618 - 5000 = 618
\]

Therefore, the interest accrued at maturity is \(\text{Final answer:}\{618\}\).
Final Answer: 6
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: The length of the ribbon was originally 30 cm. It was reduced in the ratio 5 : 3. What is its length now? # Answer option: ['A)18', 'B)30', 'C)6', 'D)15', 'E)12']
To solve this problem, we need to understand what it means to reduce the length of the ribbon in the ratio 5:3.

1. **Original Length of the Ribbon**: According to fact1, the original length of the ribbon is 30 cm.

2. **Ratio of Reduction**: According to fact2, the length of the ribbon is reduced in the ratio 5:3. This means that for every 5 units of the original length, it is now reduced to 3 units.

3. **Calculating the New Length**:
- The original length is divided into 5 parts (as per the ratio 5:3).
- Each part is \( \frac{30 \text{ cm}}{5} = 6 \text{ cm} \).
- According to the ratio, the new length will be 3 parts of this size.
- Therefore, the new length is \( 3 \times 6 \text{ cm} = 18 \text{ cm} \).

4. **Conclusion**: The length of the ribbon after reduction is 18 cm.

Thus, the final answer is: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: 64 boys and 40 girls form a group for social work. During their membership drive, the same number of boys and girls joined the group. How many members does the group have now, if the ratio of boys to girls is 4:3? # Answer option: ['A)277', 'B)288', 'C)200', 'D)277', 'E)168']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of new members who joined the group and verify the final ratio of boys to girls.

1. **Initial Group Composition:**
- Boys: 64
- Girls: 40

2. **Membership Drive:**
- The same number of boys and girls joined the group. Let's denote this number as \( x \).

3. **New Group Composition:**
- Boys: \( 64 + x \)
- Girls: \( 40 + x \)

4. **Given Ratio:**
- The ratio of boys to girls after the membership drive is 4:3.

5. **Set Up the Ratio Equation:**
\[
\frac{64 + x}{40 + x} = \frac{4}{3}
\]

6. **Cross-Multiply to Solve for \( x \):**
\[
3(64 + x) = 4(40 + x)
\]

\[
192 + 3x = 160 + 4x
\]

7. **Rearrange the Equation:**
\[
192 - 160 = 4x - 3x
\]

\[
32 = x
\]

8. **Calculate the New Total Number of Members:**
- New number of boys: \( 64 + 32 = 96 \)
- New number of girls: \( 40 + 32 = 72 \)
- Total members: \( 96 + 72 = 168 \)

9. **Verify the Ratio:**
- The ratio of boys to girls is \( \frac{96}{72} = \frac{4}{3} \), which matches the given ratio.

Therefore, the total number of members in the group now is 168.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: The events A and B are independent. The probability that event A occurs is 0.6, and the probability that at least one of the events A or B occurs is 0.96. What is the probability that event B occurs? # Answer option: ['A)0.5', 'B)0.6', 'C)0.7', 'D)0.8', 'E)0.9']
To solve this problem, we need to use the concept of independent events and the formula for the probability of the union of two events.

Given:
- Events A and B are independent.
- Probability of event A, \( P(A) = 0.6 \).
- Probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring, \( P(A \cup B) = 0.96 \).

We need to find the probability of event B, \( P(B) \).

For independent events, the probability of the union of two events is given by:
\[ P(A \cup B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A \cap B) \]

Since A and B are independent, the probability of both A and B occurring is:
\[ P(A \cap B) = P(A) \times P(B) \]

Substituting this into the formula for the union, we get:
\[ P(A \cup B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A) \times P(B) \]

We know:
\[ P(A \cup B) = 0.96 \]
\[ P(A) = 0.6 \]

Substitute these values into the equation:
\[ 0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 \times P(B)) \]

Simplify the equation:
\[ 0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6P(B) \]
\[ 0.96 = 0.6 + P(B)(1 - 0.6) \]
\[ 0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B) \]

Subtract 0.6 from both sides:
\[ 0.36 = 0.4P(B) \]

Divide both sides by 0.4 to solve for \( P(B) \):
\[ P(B) = \frac{0.36}{0.4} \]
\[ P(B) = 0.9 \]

Thus, the probability that event B occurs is 0.9.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: On a test the passing students had an average of 83, while the failing students had an average of 55. If the overall class average was 76, what percent of the class passed? # Answer option: ['A)44%', 'B)66%', 'C)68%', 'D)72%', 'E)75%']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the percentage of students who passed the test based on the given averages.

Let's denote:
- \( p \) as the percentage of students who passed.
- \( f \) as the percentage of students who failed.

Since the total percentage must add up to 100%, we have:
\[ p + f = 100 \]

We are given:
- The average score of passing students is 83.
- The average score of failing students is 55.
- The overall class average is 76.

The overall class average can be expressed as a weighted average of the passing and failing students' averages:
\[ 76 = \frac{83p + 55f}{100} \]

Substituting \( f = 100 - p \) into the equation:
\[ 76 = \frac{83p + 55(100 - p)}{100} \]

Simplify the equation:
\[ 76 = \frac{83p + 5500 - 55p}{100} \]
\[ 76 = \frac{(83p - 55p) + 5500}{100} \]
\[ 76 = \frac{28p + 5500}{100} \]

Multiply both sides by 100 to eliminate the fraction:
\[ 7600 = 28p + 5500 \]

Subtract 5500 from both sides:
\[ 2100 = 28p \]

Divide both sides by 28 to solve for \( p \):
\[ p = \frac{2100}{28} \]
\[ p = 75 \]

Thus, 75% of the class passed the test.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: In how many ways can a teacher in a kindergarten school arrange a group of 3 children (Susan, Tim and Zen) on 3 identical chairs in a straight line so that Susan is on the left of Tim? # Answer option: ['A)7', 'B)3', 'C)2', 'D)1', 'E)6']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of ways to arrange the three children, Susan, Tim, and Zen, on three identical chairs in a straight line, with the condition that Susan is on the left of Tim.

1. **Total Arrangements Without Condition:**
- First, calculate the total number of ways to arrange the three children without any conditions. Since there are 3 children, the total number of permutations is given by \(3! = 6\).

2. **Applying the Condition (Susan is on the left of Tim):**
- For each arrangement of the three children, there are two possible orders for Susan and Tim: either Susan is on the left of Tim, or Tim is on the left of Susan.
- Therefore, exactly half of the total arrangements will have Susan on the left of Tim.

3. **Calculate the Number of Valid Arrangements:**
- Since there are 6 total arrangements and half of them will have Susan on the left of Tim, the number of valid arrangements is \( \frac{6}{2} = 3\).

Thus, there are 3 ways to arrange the children such that Susan is on the left of Tim.

Question: The cross-section of a canal is shaped like a trapezium. If the canal is 10 m wide at the top and 6 m wide at the bottom and the area of cross-section is 640 square meters, the depth of cannel is? # Answer option: ['A)26', 'B)28', 'C)21', 'D)80', 'E)23']
To find the depth of the canal, we need to use the formula for the area of a trapezium (trapezoid):

\[
\text{Area} = \frac{1}{2} \times (\text{Base}_1 + \text{Base}_2) \times \text{Height}
\]

In this problem:
- \(\text{Base}_1\) (the top width) is 10 meters.
- \(\text{Base}_2\) (the bottom width) is 6 meters.
- The area of the cross-section is 640 square meters.

We need to find the height, which in this context is the depth of the canal.

Substitute the known values into the formula:

\[
640 = \frac{1}{2} \times (10 + 6) \times \text{Height}
\]

Simplify the equation:

\[
640 = \frac{1}{2} \times 16 \times \text{Height}
\]

\[
640 = 8 \times \text{Height}
\]

Now, solve for the height:

\[
\text{Height} = \frac{640}{8} = 80
\]

Therefore, the depth of the canal is 80 meters.

Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: Arjun and Sajal are friends, each has some money. If Arun gives $30 to Sajal, the Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun. But, if Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal. How much money does each have? # Answer option: ['A)62, 35', 'B)62, 34', 'C)34, 62', 'D)42, 62', 'E)62, 42']
To solve this problem, we need to set up equations based on the given facts and solve for the amounts of money Arjun and Sajal have.

Let's denote:
- \( A \) as the amount of money Arjun has.
- \( S \) as the amount of money Sajal has.

**Fact 1:** If Arjun gives $30 to Sajal, Sajal will have twice the money left with Arjun.

This can be expressed as:
\[ S + 30 = 2(A - 30) \]

**Fact 2:** If Sajal gives $10 to Arjun, Arjun will have thrice as much as is left with Sajal.

This can be expressed as:
\[ A + 10 = 3(S - 10) \]

Now, let's solve these equations step by step.

**Equation from Fact 1:**
\[ S + 30 = 2A - 60 \]
Rearrange to:
\[ S = 2A - 90 \] \[ \text{(Equation 1)} \]

**Equation from Fact 2:**
\[ A + 10 = 3S - 30 \]
Rearrange to:
\[ A = 3S - 40 \] \[ \text{(Equation 2)} \]

Now, substitute Equation 1 into Equation 2:

\[ A = 3(2A - 90) - 40 \]

Expand and simplify:
\[ A = 6A - 270 - 40 \]
\[ A = 6A - 310 \]

Rearrange to solve for \( A \):
\[ 310 = 6A - A \]
\[ 310 = 5A \]
\[ A = \frac{310}{5} \]
\[ A = 62 \]

Now that we have \( A = 62 \), substitute back into Equation 1 to find \( S \):

\[ S = 2(62) - 90 \]
\[ S = 124 - 90 \]
\[ S = 34 \]

Therefore, Arjun has $62 and Sajal has $34.

The correct answer is option B) 62, 34.

Final answer: {B}

(Two bouquets are identical whenever the number of red tulips in the two bouquets is equal and the number of white tulips in the two bouquets is equal.) # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)7', 'C)10', 'D)14', 'E)21']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the greatest number of identical bouquets that can be made using all the given tulips, with each bouquet containing the same number of white and red tulips.

We have:
- 28 white tulips
- 98 red tulips

The key is to find the greatest common divisor (GCD) of the two numbers, as this will give us the maximum number of identical bouquets we can make without leaving any tulips out.

Step 1: Find the GCD of 28 and 98.

- First, list the factors of each number:
- Factors of 28: 1, 2, 4, 7, 14, 28
- Factors of 98: 1, 2, 7, 14, 49, 98

- Identify the common factors: 1, 2, 7, 14

- The greatest common factor is 14.

Step 2: Verify that 14 is the greatest number of identical bouquets.

- If we divide the tulips into 14 bouquets, each bouquet will have:
- White tulips: 28 / 14 = 2
- Red tulips: 98 / 14 = 7

- Therefore, each bouquet will contain 2 white tulips and 7 red tulips.

Since 14 is the greatest common divisor, it is the maximum number of identical bouquets that can be made without leaving any tulips out.

Question: A flagstaff 17.5 metre high casts a shadow of length 40.25 metre. The height of building, which casts a shadow of length 28.75 metre under similar conditions will be: # Answer option: ['A)12 metre', 'B)12.5 metre', 'C)13.5 metre', 'D)14 metre', 'E)15 metre']
To solve this problem, we need to use the concept of similar triangles. When two objects cast shadows under similar conditions, the ratio of their heights is equal to the ratio of the lengths of their shadows.

Given:
- Height of the flagstaff = 17.5 meters
- Length of the flagstaff's shadow = 40.25 meters
- Length of the building's shadow = 28.75 meters

Let the height of the building be \( h \).

According to the concept of similar triangles, the ratio of the height of the flagstaff to the length of its shadow is equal to the ratio of the height of the building to the length of its shadow:

\[
\frac{17.5}{40.25} = \frac{h}{28.75}
\]

To find \( h \), we solve the equation:

\[
h = \frac{17.5 \times 28.75}{40.25}
\]

First, calculate the numerator:

\[
17.5 \times 28.75 = 503.125
\]

Now, divide by the denominator:

\[
h = \frac{503.125}{40.25} \approx 12.5
\]

Thus, the height of the building is approximately 12.5 meters.

Question: Two numbers are said to be relatively prime if they share no common positive factors other than 1. Set S contains the set of integers from 1 to 1,000, inclusive. What is the probability that a number chosen from S is relatively prime to 1,000? # Answer option: ['A)5/7', 'B)3/5', 'C)4/7', 'D)2/5', 'E)2/7']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the probability that a number chosen from the set \( S \) is relatively prime to 1,000.

**Step 1: Understand the problem**

- We are given that two numbers are relatively prime if they share no common positive factors other than 1.
- The set \( S \) contains integers from 1 to 1,000, inclusive.
- We need to find the probability that a randomly chosen number from this set is relatively prime to 1,000.

**Step 2: Prime factorization of 1,000**

First, we find the prime factorization of 1,000:

\[ 1,000 = 10^3 = (2 \times 5)^3 = 2^3 \times 5^3 \]

**Step 3: Use Euler's Totient Function**

Euler's Totient Function, \( \phi(n) \), gives the count of numbers up to \( n \) that are relatively prime to \( n \). The formula for Euler's Totient Function is:

\[ \phi(n) = n \left(1 - \frac{1}{p_1}\right)\left(1 - \frac{1}{p_2}\right)\cdots\left(1 - \frac{1}{p_m}\right) \]

where \( p_1, p_2, \ldots, p_m \) are the distinct prime factors of \( n \).

For \( n = 1,000 \), the distinct prime factors are 2 and 5. Thus, we have:

\[ \phi(1,000) = 1,000 \left(1 - \frac{1}{2}\right)\left(1 - \frac{1}{5}\right) \]

Calculating this:

\[ \phi(1,000) = 1,000 \times \frac{1}{2} \times \frac{4}{5} \]

\[ \phi(1,000) = 1,000 \times \frac{2}{5} \]

\[ \phi(1,000) = 400 \]

**Step 4: Calculate the probability**

The probability that a randomly chosen number from the set \( S \) is relatively prime to 1,000 is the ratio of the count of numbers that are relatively prime to 1,000 to the total number of numbers in the set \( S \).

The total number of numbers in \( S \) is 1,000.

Thus, the probability is:

\[ \frac{\phi(1,000)}{1,000} = \frac{400}{1,000} = \frac{2}{5} \]

**Step 5: Choose the correct answer**

The correct answer is option D) \( \frac{2}{5} \).

Final answer: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: A point on the edge of a fan blade that is rotating in a plane 10 centimeters from the center of the fan. What is the distance traveled, in centimeters, by this point after 30 seconds when the fan runs at the rate of 300 revolutions per minute? # Answer option: ['A)750pi', 'B)1500pi', 'C)1875pi', 'D)3000pi', 'E)7500pi']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the distance traveled by a point on the edge of a fan blade after 30 seconds, given the fan's rotation rate and the distance from the center.

1. **Identify the radius of the circle**: The point is 10 centimeters from the center of the fan, so the radius \( r \) of the circle is 10 cm.

2. **Calculate the circumference of the circle**: The circumference \( C \) of a circle is given by the formula:
\[
C = 2\pi r
\]
Substituting the radius:
\[
C = 2\pi \times 10 = 20\pi \text{ cm}
\]

3. **Determine the number of revolutions per second**: The fan rotates at 300 revolutions per minute. To find the number of revolutions per second, divide by 60 (since there are 60 seconds in a minute):
\[
\text{Revolutions per second} = \frac{300}{60} = 5 \text{ revolutions per second}
\]

4. **Calculate the total number of revolutions in 30 seconds**: Multiply the number of revolutions per second by the total time in seconds:
\[
\text{Total revolutions in 30 seconds} = 5 \times 30 = 150 \text{ revolutions}
\]

5. **Calculate the total distance traveled**: The distance traveled is the number of revolutions multiplied by the circumference of the circle:
\[
\text{Total distance} = 150 \times 20\pi = 3000\pi \text{ cm}
\]

Thus, the distance traveled by the point on the edge of the fan blade after 30 seconds is \( 3000\pi \) centimeters.

Question: Let A and B be independent events with P (A) = 0.2 and P(B) = 0.8. Find P(A/B)? # Answer option: ['A)0.2', 'B)0.4', 'C)0.6', 'D)1.2', 'E)1.5']
To find \( P(A/B) \), which is the probability of event A given event B, we use the formula for conditional probability:

\[
P(A/B) = \frac{P(A \cap B)}{P(B)}
\]

Since A and B are independent events, the probability of both A and B occurring is the product of their individual probabilities:

\[
P(A \cap B) = P(A) \times P(B)
\]

Given:
- \( P(A) = 0.2 \)
- \( P(B) = 0.8 \)

Calculate \( P(A \cap B) \):

\[
P(A \cap B) = 0.2 \times 0.8 = 0.16
\]

Now, substitute \( P(A \cap B) \) and \( P(B) \) into the conditional probability formula:

\[
P(A/B) = \frac{0.16}{0.8} = 0.2
\]

Thus, the probability \( P(A/B) \) is 0.2.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: A sporting goods store carries only yellow and white golf balls. At the beginning of the day it had 600 golf balls in stock, and by the end of the day it had sold 80% of its inventory of golf balls. If the store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls, and in doing so sold all of its white golf balls, how many yellow golf balls did the store have to begin the day? # Answer option: ['A)80', 'B)120', 'C)240', 'D)320', 'E)360']
To solve this problem, let's break it down step by step:

1. **Initial Inventory**: The store started with 600 golf balls in total.

2. **Golf Balls Sold**: By the end of the day, the store sold 80% of its inventory.
- 80% of 600 is calculated as follows:
\[
0.8 \times 600 = 480
\]
So, the store sold 480 golf balls.

3. **Equal Number of Yellow and White Balls Sold**: The store sold an equal number of yellow and white golf balls. Therefore, the number of yellow golf balls sold is equal to the number of white golf balls sold. Let's denote the number of each type sold as \( x \). Thus:
\[
x + x = 480 \implies 2x = 480 \implies x = 240
\]
So, the store sold 240 yellow golf balls and 240 white golf balls.

4. **All White Golf Balls Sold**: The problem states that the store sold all of its white golf balls. Therefore, the store initially had 240 white golf balls.

5. **Initial Yellow Golf Balls**: Since the total number of golf balls at the beginning of the day was 600, and 240 of them were white, the number of yellow golf balls initially is:
\[
600 - 240 = 360
\]

Thus, the store had 360 yellow golf balls at the beginning of the day.
