Question: If the probability that Stock A will increase in value during the next month is 0.56, and the probability that Stock B will increase in value during the next month is 0.74. What is the greatest value for the probability that neither of these two events will occur? # Answer option: ['A)0.22', 'B)0.26', 'C)0.37', 'D)0.46', 'E)0.63']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the greatest probability that neither Stock A nor Stock B will increase in value during the next month.

Let's denote:
- \( P(A) \) as the probability that Stock A will increase in value, which is 0.56.
- \( P(B) \) as the probability that Stock B will increase in value, which is 0.74.

We are interested in finding the probability that neither Stock A nor Stock B will increase in value. This is equivalent to finding the probability that both events do not occur, i.e., the probability that Stock A does not increase and Stock B does not increase.

The probability that Stock A does not increase is \( 1 - P(A) = 1 - 0.56 = 0.44 \).

The probability that Stock B does not increase is \( 1 - P(B) = 1 - 0.74 = 0.26 \).

To find the greatest probability that neither event occurs, we assume that the events are independent. Under this assumption, the probability that neither Stock A nor Stock B increases is the product of the probabilities that each does not increase:

\[ P(\text{Neither A nor B}) = P(\text{Not A}) \times P(\text{Not B}) = 0.44 \times 0.26. \]

Calculating this gives:

\[ 0.44 \times 0.26 = 0.1144. \]

However, the problem asks for the greatest value for the probability that neither of these two events will occur. The greatest value occurs when the events are mutually exclusive, meaning they cannot both happen at the same time. In this case, the probability that neither event occurs is:

\[ 1 - \max(P(A), P(B)) = 1 - 0.74 = 0.26. \]

Thus, the greatest probability that neither Stock A nor Stock B will increase in value is 0.26.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b

Question: M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D. If 3 men drop out how much more will each have to contribute towards the purchase of the gift? # Answer option: ['A)D/(M-3)', 'B)MD/3', 'C)M/(D-3)', 'D)3D/(M2-3M)', 'E)None of these']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how much more each remaining man will have to contribute if 3 men drop out from the original group of M men.

1. **Initial Contribution:**
- Originally, M men agree to purchase a gift for Rs. D.
- Therefore, the initial contribution per man is \( \frac{D}{M} \).

2. **After 3 Men Drop Out:**
- If 3 men drop out, the number of men left is \( M - 3 \).
- The total cost of the gift remains Rs. D.
- Therefore, the new contribution per man is \( \frac{D}{M-3} \).

3. **Additional Contribution Required:**
- The additional contribution required per man is the difference between the new contribution and the initial contribution.
- This is calculated as:
\[
\text{Additional Contribution} = \frac{D}{M-3} - \frac{D}{M}
\]

4. **Simplifying the Expression:**
- To simplify the expression, find a common denominator, which is \( M(M-3) \):
\[
\frac{D}{M-3} - \frac{D}{M} = \frac{D \cdot M - D \cdot (M-3)}{M(M-3)}
\]
- Simplify the numerator:
\[
D \cdot M - D \cdot (M-3) = D \cdot M - D \cdot M + 3D = 3D
\]
- Therefore, the expression becomes:
\[
\frac{3D}{M(M-3)}
\]

5. **Final Answer:**
- The additional contribution required per man is \( \frac{3D}{M(M-3)} \).
- This matches with option D) \( \frac{3D}{M^2-3M} \).

Thus, the final answer is: {D}
Final Answer: d
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: Fernando purchased a university meal plan that allows him to have a total of 3 lunches and 3 dinners per week. If the cafeteria is closed on weekends and Fernando always goes home for a dinner on Friday nights, how many options does he have to allocate his meals? # Answer option: ['A)5C3*4C3', 'B)5C4*4C2', 'C)5C2*4C4', 'D)5C6*4C5', 'E)4C3*4C3']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how Fernando can allocate his 3 lunches and 3 dinners during the weekdays, given the constraints.

1. **Understanding the constraints:**
- Fernando has 5 weekdays (Monday to Friday) to allocate his meals.
- He has 3 lunches and 3 dinners to allocate.
- The cafeteria is closed on weekends, so all meals must be allocated from Monday to Friday.
- Fernando always goes home for dinner on Friday nights, so he cannot have a cafeteria dinner on Friday.

2. **Allocating lunches:**
- Fernando needs to choose 3 days out of the 5 weekdays to have his lunches. This is a combination problem where we choose 3 days from 5, which is calculated as \( \binom{5}{3} \).

3. **Allocating dinners:**
- Since Fernando goes home for dinner on Friday, he can only have dinners on Monday to Thursday.
- He needs to choose 3 days out of these 4 days to have his dinners. This is another combination problem where we choose 3 days from 4, which is calculated as \( \binom{4}{3} \).

4. **Calculating the total number of options:**
- The total number of ways to allocate the lunches and dinners is the product of the two combinations: \( \binom{5}{3} \times \binom{4}{3} \).

5. **Matching with the answer options:**
- The expression \( \binom{5}{3} \times \binom{4}{3} \) corresponds to the answer option 'A)5C3*4C3'.

Therefore, the final answer is: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount. How many times did the coin landed on Heads? # Answer option: ['A)10', 'B)23', 'C)16', 'D)18', 'E)12']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how many times the coin landed on heads such that neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any money after 20 flips.

Let's define:
- \( H \) as the number of times the coin lands on heads.
- \( T \) as the number of times the coin lands on tails.

From the problem, we know:
1. The total number of flips is 20, so \( H + T = 20 \).
2. The amount of money exchanged is such that neither wins or loses any money, which means the total money given by Christopher to Jonathan equals the total money given by Jonathan to Christopher.

The money exchanged can be expressed as:
- Christopher gives Jonathan $2 for each head, so he gives \( 2H \) dollars in total.
- Jonathan gives Christopher $3 for each tail, so he gives \( 3T \) dollars in total.

Since neither wins or loses any money, the total money exchanged must be equal:
\[ 2H = 3T \]

Now we have two equations:
1. \( H + T = 20 \)
2. \( 2H = 3T \)

We can solve these equations simultaneously. From the second equation, express \( T \) in terms of \( H \):
\[ T = \frac{2H}{3} \]

Substitute this expression for \( T \) into the first equation:
\[ H + \frac{2H}{3} = 20 \]

Multiply through by 3 to eliminate the fraction:
\[ 3H + 2H = 60 \]
\[ 5H = 60 \]
\[ H = 12 \]

Thus, the coin landed on heads 12 times.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: In a row of children Neha is 12th from left end and Radha is 6th from right end. When Radha is shifted to left by 2 places and Neha is shifted to right by 2 places there 6 children between Radha and Neha. How many children are there in the row? # Answer option: ['A)23', 'B)27', 'C)26', 'D)28', 'E)29']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the total number of children in the row based on the given facts.

1. **Initial Positions:**
- Neha is 12th from the left end.
- Radha is 6th from the right end.

2. **Shifts:**
- Radha is shifted 2 places to the left. So, her new position is 6 + 2 = 8th from the right end.
- Neha is shifted 2 places to the right. So, her new position is 12 + 2 = 14th from the left end.

3. **Position Relationship:**
- After the shifts, there are 6 children between Radha and Neha.

4. **Calculate the Total Number of Children:**
- Neha's new position is 14th from the left.
- Radha's new position is 8th from the right.
- The number of children between Neha and Radha is 6.

Let's denote the total number of children as \( N \).

Since Radha is 8th from the right, her position from the left is \( N - 8 + 1 \).

According to the problem, the number of children between Neha and Radha is 6. Therefore, we can set up the equation:

\[
(N - 8 + 1) - 14 = 6
\]

Simplifying the equation:

\[
N - 7 - 14 = 6
\]

\[
N - 21 = 6
\]

\[
N = 27
\]

Thus, the total number of children in the row is 27.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: A car is being driven, in a straight line and at a uniform speed, towards the base of a vertical tower. The top of the tower is observed from the car and, in the process, it takes 10 minutes for the angle of elevation to change from 45° to 60°. After how much more time will this car reach the base of the tower? # Answer option: ['A)5(√3 + 1)', 'B)6(√3 + √2)', 'C)7(√3 – 1)', 'D)8(√3 – 2)', 'E)None of these']
To solve this problem, we need to use trigonometry and the concept of relative speed. Let's break it down step by step:

1. **Understanding the Problem:**
- A car is moving towards a tower.
- The angle of elevation from the car to the top of the tower changes from 45° to 60° in 10 minutes.
- We need to find out how much more time it will take for the car to reach the base of the tower.

2. **Trigonometric Setup:**
- Let the height of the tower be \( h \).
- Let the initial distance from the car to the base of the tower when the angle is 45° be \( d_1 \).
- Let the distance from the car to the base of the tower when the angle is 60° be \( d_2 \).

3. **Using Trigonometry:**
- When the angle of elevation is 45°, we have:
\[
\tan(45°) = \frac{h}{d_1} \implies d_1 = h
\]
- When the angle of elevation is 60°, we have:
\[
\tan(60°) = \frac{h}{d_2} \implies d_2 = \frac{h}{\sqrt{3}}
\]

4. **Distance Travelled:**
- The car travels from \( d_1 \) to \( d_2 \) in 10 minutes.
- The distance travelled in 10 minutes is:
\[
d_1 - d_2 = h - \frac{h}{\sqrt{3}} = h \left(1 - \frac{1}{\sqrt{3}}\right) = h \left(\frac{\sqrt{3} - 1}{\sqrt{3}}\right)
\]

5. **Speed of the Car:**
- The speed of the car is the distance travelled divided by time:
\[
\text{Speed} = \frac{h \left(\frac{\sqrt{3} - 1}{\sqrt{3}}\right)}{10}
\]

6. **Time to Reach the Base:**
- The remaining distance to the base of the tower is \( d_2 \).
- The time to cover this distance at the same speed is:
\[
\text{Time} = \frac{d_2}{\text{Speed}} = \frac{\frac{h}{\sqrt{3}}}{\frac{h \left(\frac{\sqrt{3} - 1}{\sqrt{3}}\right)}{10}}
\]
- Simplifying this expression:
\[
\text{Time} = \frac{\frac{h}{\sqrt{3}} \cdot 10}{h \left(\frac{\sqrt{3} - 1}{\sqrt{3}}\right)} = \frac{10}{\sqrt{3} - 1}
\]

7. **Rationalizing the Denominator:**
- Multiply numerator and denominator by the conjugate of the denominator:
\[
\frac{10}{\sqrt{3} - 1} \cdot \frac{\sqrt{3} + 1}{\sqrt{3} + 1} = \frac{10(\sqrt{3} + 1)}{(\sqrt{3})^2 - 1^2} = \frac{10(\sqrt{3} + 1)}{3 - 1} = 5(\sqrt{3} + 1)
\]

8. **Final Answer:**
- The time it will take for the car to reach the base of the tower is \( 5(\sqrt{3} + 1) \).

Therefore, the correct answer is option A.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: Anna has 4 books. If she decide to arrange the 4 books in every possible combination and moved just one book every minute, how long would it taken by her? # Answer option: ['A)22 minutes', 'B)30 minutes', 'C)15 minutes', 'D)24 minutes', 'E)35 minutes']
To determine how long it would take Anna to arrange her 4 books in every possible combination, we need to calculate the number of permutations of the 4 books.

The number of permutations of \( n \) distinct items is given by \( n! \) (n factorial), which is the product of all positive integers up to \( n \).

For 4 books, the number of permutations is:
\[ 4! = 4 \times 3 \times 2 \times 1 = 24 \]

This means there are 24 different ways to arrange the 4 books.

According to , Anna moves just one book every minute. Therefore, it would take her 1 minute to complete each arrangement.

Since there are 24 different arrangements, it would take Anna 24 minutes to arrange the books in every possible combination.

Thus, the correct answer is 24 minutes.

Question: X and Y are two alloys which were made by mixing zinc and copper in the ratio 6:9 and 7:11, respectively. If 40 grams of alloy X and 60 grams of alloy Y are melted and mixed to form alloy Z, what is the ratio of zinc and copper in the alloy Z? # Answer option: ['A)69:91', 'B)59:91', 'C)59:90', 'D)59:91', 'E)69:101']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the amount of zinc and copper in alloys X and Y, and then find the ratio of zinc to copper in the new alloy Z formed by mixing them.

**Step 1: Determine the composition of alloy X.**

Alloy X is made by mixing zinc and copper in the ratio 6:9. This can be simplified to 2:3.

- Total parts in alloy X = 2 (zinc) + 3 (copper) = 5 parts.
- Zinc in alloy X = \(\frac{2}{5}\) of the total weight.
- Copper in alloy X = \(\frac{3}{5}\) of the total weight.

Given that we have 40 grams of alloy X:
- Zinc in 40 grams of alloy X = \(\frac{2}{5} \times 40 = 16\) grams.
- Copper in 40 grams of alloy X = \(\frac{3}{5} \times 40 = 24\) grams.

**Step 2: Determine the composition of alloy Y.**

Alloy Y is made by mixing zinc and copper in the ratio 7:11.

- Total parts in alloy Y = 7 (zinc) + 11 (copper) = 18 parts.
- Zinc in alloy Y = \(\frac{7}{18}\) of the total weight.
- Copper in alloy Y = \(\frac{11}{18}\) of the total weight.

Given that we have 60 grams of alloy Y:
- Zinc in 60 grams of alloy Y = \(\frac{7}{18} \times 60 = 23.33\) grams.
- Copper in 60 grams of alloy Y = \(\frac{11}{18} \times 60 = 36.67\) grams.

**Step 3: Combine the amounts to form alloy Z.**

Now, we combine the zinc and copper from both alloys to form alloy Z.

- Total zinc in alloy Z = 16 grams (from X) + 23.33 grams (from Y) = 39.33 grams.
- Total copper in alloy Z = 24 grams (from X) + 36.67 grams (from Y) = 60.67 grams.

**Step 4: Calculate the ratio of zinc to copper in alloy Z.**

The ratio of zinc to copper in alloy Z is:
\[
\text{Ratio} = \frac{39.33}{60.67}
\]

To simplify this, we can multiply both the numerator and the denominator by 3 to avoid decimals:
- Zinc: \(39.33 \times 3 = 118\)
- Copper: \(60.67 \times 3 = 182\)

Thus, the ratio of zinc to copper in alloy Z is approximately 118:182, which simplifies to 59:91.

Therefore, the final answer is: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: M = abc is a three digit number and N = cba, if M > N and M - N + 396c = 990. Then how many values of M are more than 300. # Answer option: ['A)20', 'B)30', 'C)40', 'D)200', 'E)None']
To solve this problem, we need to analyze the given facts and equations.

1. **Understanding the numbers M and N:**
- \( M = 100a + 10b + c \) (since M is a three-digit number with digits a, b, and c)
- \( N = 100c + 10b + a \) (since N is the number formed by reversing the digits of M)

2. **Given conditions:**
- \( M > N \)
- \( M - N + 396c = 990 \)

3. **Expressing M - N:**
\[
M - N = (100a + 10b + c) - (100c + 10b + a) = 99a - 99c = 99(a - c)
\]

4. **Substituting into the equation:**
\[
99(a - c) + 396c = 990
\]

5. **Simplifying the equation:**
\[
99(a - c) + 396c = 990 \implies 99a - 99c + 396c = 990
\]
\[
99a + 297c = 990
\]
\[
99a = 990 - 297c
\]
\[
a = \frac{990 - 297c}{99}
\]

6. **Simplifying further:**
\[
a = \frac{990}{99} - \frac{297c}{99}
\]
\[
a = 10 - 3c
\]

7. **Finding valid values for a and c:**
- Since a is a digit (1 to 9 for a three-digit number), and c is a digit (0 to 9), we need to find integer solutions for \( a = 10 - 3c \).

8. **Checking possible values of c:**
- If \( c = 0 \), then \( a = 10 \) (not valid since a must be a single digit)
- If \( c = 1 \), then \( a = 7 \)
- If \( c = 2 \), then \( a = 4 \)
- If \( c = 3 \), then \( a = 1 \)
- If \( c \geq 4 \), then \( a \) becomes negative or zero, which is not valid.

9. **Valid pairs (a, c):**
- (7, 1), (4, 2), (1, 3)

10. **Calculating M for each valid pair:**
- For (7, 1): \( M = 100 \times 7 + 10b + 1 = 701 + 10b \)
- For (4, 2): \( M = 100 \times 4 + 10b + 2 = 402 + 10b \)
- For (1, 3): \( M = 100 \times 1 + 10b + 3 = 103 + 10b \)

11. **Finding values of M greater than 300:**
- For (7, 1): \( M = 701 + 10b \) (all values are greater than 300)
- For (4, 2): \( M = 402 + 10b \) (all values are greater than 300)
- For (1, 3): \( M = 103 + 10b \) (none are greater than 300)

12. **Counting the number of valid M values:**
- For (7, 1): \( b \) can be 0 to 9, giving 10 values.
- For (4, 2): \( b \) can be 0 to 9, giving 10 values.
- Total = 10 + 10 = 20 values.

Therefore, the number of values of M that are more than 300 is 20.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile. # Answer option: ['A)11.75 miles', 'B)12.75 miles', 'C)17.75 miles', 'D)14.75 miles', 'E)10.75 miles']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how far you can travel with $8.50 in a cab that charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter-mile.

1. **Initial Charge:**
- The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile.
- Subtract this from the total amount you have: $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00 remaining.

2. **Cost for Additional Distance:**
- Each additional quarter-mile costs 10 cents.
- With $5.00 remaining, calculate how many additional quarter-miles you can afford: $5.00 / $0.10 = 50 additional quarter-miles.

3. **Total Distance Calculation:**
- The first quarter-mile is already covered by the initial charge.
- You can travel 50 additional quarter-miles with the remaining money.
- Total quarter-miles = 1 (initial) + 50 (additional) = 51 quarter-miles.

4. **Convert Quarter-Miles to Miles:**
- There are 4 quarter-miles in a mile.
- Total miles = 51 quarter-miles / 4 = 12.75 miles.

Therefore, the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 is 12.75 miles.

Question: A square piece of cloth is trimmed by 4 feet on one edge to form a rectangular piece, which is then cut diagonally in half to create two triangles. If the area of each of triangle is 70 square feet, what was the perimeter (in feet) of the original piece of square cloth? # Answer option: ['A)56', 'B)58', 'C)60', 'D)62', 'E)64']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the side length of the original square piece of cloth and then calculate its perimeter.

1. **Understanding the Problem:**
- We start with a square piece of cloth.
- One edge of the square is trimmed by 4 feet to form a rectangle.
- This rectangle is then cut diagonally to form two triangles.
- The area of each triangle is given as 70 square feet.

2. **Setting Up the Equations:**
- Let the side length of the original square be \( s \).
- After trimming 4 feet from one edge, the dimensions of the rectangle become \( s \) (original side) and \( s - 4 \) (trimmed side).
- The area of the rectangle is \( s \times (s - 4) \).

3. **Area of the Triangles:**
- The rectangle is cut diagonally to form two right-angled triangles.
- The area of each triangle is half the area of the rectangle.
- Therefore, the area of the rectangle is \( 2 \times 70 = 140 \) square feet.

4. **Formulating the Equation:**
- The area of the rectangle is given by:
\[
s \times (s - 4) = 140
\]
- Expanding and rearranging gives:
\[
s^2 - 4s = 140
\]
- Rearranging further:
\[
s^2 - 4s - 140 = 0
\]

5. **Solving the Quadratic Equation:**
- We solve the quadratic equation \( s^2 - 4s - 140 = 0 \) using the quadratic formula:
\[
s = \frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}
\]
- Here, \( a = 1 \), \( b = -4 \), and \( c = -140 \).
- Calculate the discriminant:
\[
b^2 - 4ac = (-4)^2 - 4 \times 1 \times (-140) = 16 + 560 = 576
\]
- The square root of 576 is 24.
- Therefore, the solutions for \( s \) are:
\[
s = \frac{4 \pm 24}{2}
\]
- This gives \( s = 14 \) or \( s = -10 \). Since a side length cannot be negative, \( s = 14 \).

6. **Calculating the Perimeter:**
- The perimeter of the original square is \( 4 \times s = 4 \times 14 = 56 \) feet.

Final answer: \(\{A\}\)
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: The manufacturer of tyres is offering a 20% discount on the price of its tubeless tyres. Some retailers are offering additional discounts. If a retailer offers an additional 20% discount, then what is the total discount available at that retailer? # Answer option: ['A)10%', 'B)25%', 'C)28%', 'D)30%', 'E)36%']
To determine the total discount available at the retailer, we need to consider both the manufacturer's discount and the additional discount offered by the retailer.

1. **Manufacturer's Discount:**
- The manufacturer offers a 20% discount on the original price of the tubeless tyres.

2. **Retailer's Additional Discount:**
- The retailer offers an additional 20% discount on the price after the manufacturer's discount has been applied.

Let's calculate the effective total discount step by step:

- **Step 1:** Calculate the price after the manufacturer's discount.
- Let the original price of the tyres be \( P \).
- After a 20% manufacturer's discount, the price becomes \( P - 0.20P = 0.80P \).

- **Step 2:** Calculate the price after the retailer's additional discount.
- The retailer offers a 20% discount on the price after the manufacturer's discount, which is \( 0.80P \).
- The additional discount is \( 0.20 \times 0.80P = 0.16P \).
- Therefore, the price after the retailer's discount is \( 0.80P - 0.16P = 0.64P \).

- **Step 3:** Calculate the total discount.
- The total discount is the reduction from the original price \( P \) to the final price \( 0.64P \).
- The total discount amount is \( P - 0.64P = 0.36P \).
- Therefore, the total discount percentage is \( \frac{0.36P}{P} \times 100\% = 36\% \).

Thus, the total discount available at the retailer is 36%.

Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: Consider there is an staircase elevator and you are coming down. If you walk 20 steps and stop, then you reach bottom in 10 minutes. If you walk 10 steps and stop, you reach to the ground in 20 minutes. What is the speed of the elevator? # Answer option: ['A)1 step/minute', 'B)2 step/minute', 'C)3 step/minute', 'D)4 step/minute', 'E)None of the above']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the speed of the elevator in steps per minute. Let's analyze the given facts:

1. **Fact 1**: If you walk 20 steps and stop, you reach the bottom in 10 minutes.
2. **Fact 2**: If you walk 10 steps and stop, you reach the ground in 20 minutes.

Let's denote:
- \( v \) as the speed of the elevator in steps per minute.
- \( S \) as the total number of steps from the top to the bottom.

### Analyzing Fact 1:
- You walk 20 steps, so the elevator covers \( S - 20 \) steps.
- The time taken to reach the bottom is 10 minutes.
- Therefore, the elevator covers \( S - 20 \) steps in 10 minutes.

The equation for Fact 1 is:
\[ S - 20 = 10v \]

### Analyzing Fact 2:
- You walk 10 steps, so the elevator covers \( S - 10 \) steps.
- The time taken to reach the bottom is 20 minutes.
- Therefore, the elevator covers \( S - 10 \) steps in 20 minutes.

The equation for Fact 2 is:
\[ S - 10 = 20v \]

### Solving the Equations:
We have two equations:
1. \( S - 20 = 10v \)
2. \( S - 10 = 20v \)

Subtract the first equation from the second:
\[ (S - 10) - (S - 20) = 20v - 10v \]
\[ 10 = 10v \]
\[ v = 1 \]

Thus, the speed of the elevator is 1 step per minute.

### Final Answer:
The correct answer is option A) 1 step/minute.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: A man borrows Rs.360. If he pays it back in 12 monthly installments of Rs.31.50, what is his interest rate? # Answer option: ['A)1.5%', 'B)4.5%', 'C)10%', 'D)5%', 'E)12%']
To find the interest rate, we need to determine the total interest paid and then calculate the rate based on the principal amount.

1. **Calculate the Total Amount Paid:**
- The man pays Rs.31.50 per month for 12 months.
- Total amount paid = 31.50 * 12 = Rs.378.

2. **Calculate the Total Interest Paid:**
- The principal amount borrowed is Rs.360.
- Total interest paid = Total amount paid - Principal = 378 - 360 = Rs.18.

3. **Calculate the Interest Rate:**
- The interest rate is calculated on the principal for one year.
- Interest rate = (Total interest / Principal) * 100
- Interest rate = (18 / 360) * 100 = 5%.

Therefore, the interest rate is 5%.

Question: My wall contains 8 red colour ties, 13 violet colour ties, 10 blue colour ties, 5 pink colour ties, 4 green colour ties. If electricity is gone and I want at least two ties of same colour then how many ties I should take out from my rack? # Answer option: ['A)2', 'B)3', 'C)4', 'D)5', 'E)6']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the minimum number of ties you must take out to ensure that you have at least two ties of the same color. This is a classic problem that can be approached using the Pigeonhole Principle.

Let's break it down step by step:

1. **Identify the different colors and their quantities:**
- Red: 8 ties
- Violet: 13 ties
- Blue: 10 ties
- Pink: 5 ties
- Green: 4 ties

2. **Apply the Pigeonhole Principle:**
- The Pigeonhole Principle states that if you have more items than containers, at least one container must contain more than one item.
- In this context, the "containers" are the colors, and the "items" are the ties.

3. **Determine the worst-case scenario:**
- To avoid having two ties of the same color, you would need to pick one tie of each color first. This means picking 5 ties (one of each color: red, violet, blue, pink, and green).

4. **Ensure at least two ties of the same color:**
- After picking one tie of each color (5 ties), the next tie you pick (the 6th tie) will definitely be a duplicate of one of the colors you have already picked.

Therefore, to guarantee that you have at least two ties of the same color, you need to take out a minimum of 6 ties.

Question: A hollow cube of size 5cm is taken, with the thickness of 1cm. It is made of smaller cubes of size 1cm. If the outer surface of the cube is painted, how many faces of the smaller cubes remain unpainted? # Answer option: ['A)438', 'B)550', 'C)500', 'D)450', 'E)498']
To solve this problem, we need to analyze the structure of the hollow cube and determine how many faces of the smaller cubes remain unpainted after the outer surface is painted.

1. **Understanding the Structure:**
- The hollow cube has an outer size of 5 cm and a thickness of 1 cm.
- This means the inner cube (the hollow part) has a size of \(5 - 2 \times 1 = 3\) cm, because the thickness is subtracted from both sides.

2. **Number of Smaller Cubes:**
- The entire cube is made up of smaller cubes of size 1 cm.
- The outer cube (5 cm) consists of \(5 \times 5 \times 5 = 125\) smaller cubes.
- The inner hollow part (3 cm) consists of \(3 \times 3 \times 3 = 27\) smaller cubes.

3. **Cubes in the Shell:**
- The number of smaller cubes that form the shell (the part that is not hollow) is the difference between the total number of cubes in the outer cube and the inner hollow part: \(125 - 27 = 98\).

4. **Painting the Outer Surface:**
- When the outer surface is painted, only the cubes on the outermost layer are affected.
- The outermost layer consists of the cubes on the surface of the 5 cm cube.

5. **Unpainted Faces:**
- Each smaller cube has 6 faces.
- When the outer surface is painted, only the outer faces of the outermost layer are painted.
- The cubes that are not on the outermost layer will have all their faces unpainted.
- The inner hollow part (3 cm cube) is not painted at all, so all its faces remain unpainted.

6. **Calculating Unpainted Faces:**
- The inner hollow part consists of 27 smaller cubes, each with 6 unpainted faces.
- Therefore, the total number of unpainted faces is \(27 \times 6 = 162\).

7. **Considering the Shell:**
- The shell consists of 98 smaller cubes.
- The cubes on the outermost layer of the shell will have some faces painted, but the inner faces (facing the hollow part) will remain unpainted.
- The cubes on the inner surface of the shell (facing the hollow part) will have 5 faces unpainted (since only the face exposed to the outer surface is painted).

8. **Calculating Unpainted Faces in the Shell:**
- The inner surface of the shell (the part facing the hollow cube) consists of a 3 cm cube, which is \(3 \times 3 \times 3 = 27\) cubes.
- Each of these 27 cubes has 5 unpainted faces.
- Therefore, the total number of unpainted faces in the shell is \(27 \times 5 = 135\).

9. **Total Unpainted Faces:**
- The total number of unpainted faces is the sum of unpainted faces from the hollow part and the shell: \(162 + 135 = 297\).

However, it seems there is a mistake in the calculation. Let's re-evaluate:

- The inner hollow part (3 cm cube) has 27 cubes, each with 6 unpainted faces: \(27 \times 6 = 162\).
- The shell has 98 cubes, but only the inner surface of the shell (facing the hollow part) will have unpainted faces.

Question: Q is as much younger than R as he is older than T. If the sum of the ages of R and T is 50 years. What is definitely the difference between R and Q's age? # Answer option: ['A)22', 'B)27', 'C)29', 'D)Cannot be determined', 'E)None of the above']
To solve this problem, let's define the ages of Q, R, and T as follows:

- Let Q's age be \( q \).
- Let R's age be \( r \).
- Let T's age be \( t \).

From the first fact, we know that Q is as much younger than R as he is older than T. This can be expressed as:

\[ r - q = q - t \]

This equation implies that the difference between R's age and Q's age is equal to the difference between Q's age and T's age.

Rearranging the equation, we get:

\[ r - q = q - t \]
\[ r + t = 2q \]

From the second fact, we know that the sum of the ages of R and T is 50 years:

\[ r + t = 50 \]

Now, we have two equations:

1. \( r + t = 2q \)
2. \( r + t = 50 \)

Since both expressions for \( r + t \) are equal, we can set them equal to each other:

\[ 2q = 50 \]

Solving for \( q \), we get:

\[ q = 25 \]

Now, we need to find the difference between R's age and Q's age, which is \( r - q \).

From the equation \( r + t = 50 \) and \( r + t = 2q \), we know:

\[ r + t = 50 \]
\[ r + t = 2 \times 25 = 50 \]

This confirms that our calculations are consistent. However, we need to find \( r - q \).

From the equation \( r - q = q - t \), we substitute \( q = 25 \):

\[ r - 25 = 25 - t \]

Rearranging gives:

\[ r = 50 - t \]

Substituting back into the equation \( r + t = 50 \):

\[ (50 - t) + t = 50 \]

This equation is always true, but it doesn't directly give us \( r - q \).

However, since \( r + t = 50 \) and \( r + t = 2q \), we know that:

\[ r - q = q - t \]

And since \( q = 25 \), we can substitute:

\[ r - 25 = 25 - t \]

Thus, the difference \( r - q \) is equal to \( q - t \), which is:

\[ r - q = 25 - t \]

Since \( r + t = 50 \), we can express \( t \) in terms of \( r \):

\[ t = 50 - r \]

Substituting back, we get:

\[ r - q = 25 - (50 - r) \]
\[ r - q = 25 - 50 + r \]
\[ r - q = r - 25 \]

This simplifies to:

\[ r - q = 25 - t \]

Since \( r + t = 50 \), we have:

\[ r - q = 25 - (50 - r) \]
\[ r - q = r - 25 \]

Thus, the difference between R and Q's age is:

\[ r - q = 25 - t \]

Since \( r + t = 50 \), we have:

\[ r - q = 25 - (50 - r) \]
\[ r - q = r - 25 \]

Therefore, the difference between R and Q's age is 0, which means:

\[ r - q = 0 \]

Question: While selling a watch, a shopkeeper gives a discount of 5%. If he gives a discount of 7%, he earns Rs. 15 less as profit. The marked price of the watch is: # Answer option: ['A)Rs. 697.50', 'B)Rs. 712.50', 'C)Rs. 787.50', 'D)Rs. 750', 'E)Rs. 780']
To solve this problem, let's define the variables and work through the steps:

1. **Define Variables:**
- Let \( M \) be the marked price of the watch.
- Let \( C \) be the cost price of the watch.
- The profit is the difference between the selling price and the cost price.

2. **Discount Calculations:**
- With a 5% discount, the selling price is \( 0.95M \).
- With a 7% discount, the selling price is \( 0.93M \).

3. **Profit Calculations:**
- Profit with a 5% discount: \( 0.95M - C \).
- Profit with a 7% discount: \( 0.93M - C \).

4. **Given Condition:**
- The profit difference between the two scenarios is Rs. 15.
- Therefore, \( (0.95M - C) - (0.93M - C) = 15 \).

5. **Simplify the Equation:**
- \( 0.95M - 0.93M = 15 \).
- \( 0.02M = 15 \).

6. **Solve for \( M \):**
- \( M = \frac{15}{0.02} \).
- \( M = 750 \).

Thus, the marked price of the watch is Rs. 750.

To solve this problem, we need to determine the distance from Winson's home to his school, given the speeds and total time for the round trip.

Let's denote the distance from Winson's home to his school as \( d \) miles.

1. **Running to School:**
- Speed = 10 miles/hr
- Time taken to run to school = \( \frac{d}{10} \) hours

2. **Walking Home:**
- Speed = 5 miles/hr
- Time taken to walk home = \( \frac{d}{5} \) hours

3. **Total Time for the Journey:**
- The total time for the round trip is given as 1 hour.
- Therefore, the equation for the total time is:
\[
\frac{d}{10} + \frac{d}{5} = 1
\]

4. **Solve the Equation:**
- First, find a common denominator for the fractions, which is 10.
- Rewrite the equation:
\[
\frac{d}{10} + \frac{2d}{10} = 1
\]
- Combine the fractions:
\[
\frac{3d}{10} = 1
\]
- Solve for \( d \):

3d = 10

\[

\[

Question: If 36 ≤ n ≤ 72, then x = (n^2 + 2√n(n + 4) + 16) / (n + 4√n + 4) satisfies # Answer option: ['A)20 < x < 54', 'B)23 < x < 58', 'C)25 < x < 64', 'D)28 < x < 60', 'E)None of these']
To solve this problem, we need to analyze the expression for \( x \) given by:

\[
x = \frac{n^2 + 2\sqrt{n}(n + 4) + 16}{n + 4\sqrt{n} + 4}
\]

First, let's simplify the expression for \( x \).

### Step 1: Simplify the numerator

The numerator is:

\[
n^2 + 2\sqrt{n}(n + 4) + 16
\]

This can be rewritten as:

\[
n^2 + 2n\sqrt{n} + 8\sqrt{n} + 16
\]

### Step 2: Simplify the denominator

The denominator is:

\[
n + 4\sqrt{n} + 4
\]

### Step 3: Simplify the expression

Notice that the numerator can be rewritten as a perfect square:

\[
(n + 4\sqrt{n} + 4)^2 = n^2 + 2n\sqrt{n} + 8\sqrt{n} + 16
\]

Thus, the expression for \( x \) simplifies to:

\[
x = \frac{(n + 4\sqrt{n} + 4)^2}{n + 4\sqrt{n} + 4} = n + 4\sqrt{n} + 4
\]

### Step 4: Analyze the range of \( x \)

Given \( 36 \leq n \leq 72 \), we need to find the range of \( x = n + 4\sqrt{n} + 4 \).

- For \( n = 36 \):
\[
x = 36 + 4\sqrt{36} + 4 = 36 + 24 + 4 = 64
\]

- For \( n = 72 \):
\[
x = 72 + 4\sqrt{72} + 4
\]

Calculate \( \sqrt{72} \):
\[
\sqrt{72} = \sqrt{36 \times 2} = 6\sqrt{2} \approx 6 \times 1.414 = 8.484
\]

Therefore:
\[
x \approx 72 + 4 \times 8.484 + 4 = 72 + 33.936 + 4 = 109.936
\]

### Step 5: Determine the correct answer

The range of \( x \) is approximately \( 64 \leq x \leq 109.936 \).

Now, compare this range with the given options:

- A) \( 20 < x < 54 \)
- B) \( 23 < x < 58 \)
- C) \( 25 < x < 64 \)
- D) \( 28 < x < 60 \)
- E) None of these

The range \( 64 \leq x \leq 109.936 \) does not fit any of the given options A, B, C, or D.

Therefore, the correct answer is:

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: At my favorite fruit stand, an orange costs 18 dollars, a pineapple costs 27 dollars, and a grape costs 15 dollars. Using the same logic, can you tell how much a mango costs? # Answer option: ['A)22 dollars', 'B)15 dollars', 'C)20 dollars', 'D)18 dollars', 'E)10 dollars']
To solve this problem, we need to identify the pattern or logic used to determine the cost of each fruit. Let's analyze the given facts:

1. An orange costs 18 dollars.
2. A pineapple costs 27 dollars.
3. A grape costs 15 dollars.

We need to find a consistent pattern or rule that applies to these prices. One possible approach is to consider the number of letters in each fruit's name:

- "Orange" has 6 letters.
- "Pineapple" has 9 letters.
- "Grape" has 5 letters.

Now, let's see if there's a relationship between the number of letters and the cost:

- Orange: 6 letters, 18 dollars. (18 / 6 = 3)
- Pineapple: 9 letters, 27 dollars. (27 / 9 = 3)
- Grape: 5 letters, 15 dollars. (15 / 5 = 3)

In each case, the cost of the fruit is 3 times the number of letters in its name.

Now, let's apply this logic to determine the cost of a mango:

- "Mango" has 5 letters.

Using the same pattern, the cost of a mango would be 5 letters * 3 dollars per letter = 15 dollars.

Therefore, the cost of a mango is 15 dollars.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b

Question: Julie’s yard is rectangular. One side of the yard is 100 feet wide. The total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet. What is the length of the other side of the yard? # Answer option: ['A)30 feet', 'B)20 feet', 'C)10 feet', 'D)50 feet', 'E)60 feet']
To find the length of the other side of Julie's rectangular yard, we can use the formula for the area of a rectangle, which is:

\[
\text{Area} = \text{length} \times \text{width}
\]

From the problem, we know:

- The width of the yard is 100 feet (from fact1).
- The total area of the yard is 3,000 square feet (from fact2).

Let's denote the length of the other side of the yard as \( L \).

Using the area formula, we have:

\[
3,000 = L \times 100
\]

To solve for \( L \), divide both sides of the equation by 100:

\[
L = \frac{3,000}{100} = 30
\]

Therefore, the length of the other side of the yard is 30 feet.

Now, let's match this with the answer options provided:

- A) 30 feet
- B) 20 feet
- C) 10 feet
- D) 50 feet
- E) 60 feet

The correct answer is option A) 30 feet.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: Alice wants to put up fencing around three sides of her rectangular yard and leave one side of 10 meters unfenced. If the yard has an area of 240 square meters, how many meters of fencing does she need? # Answer option: ['A)58', 'B)62', 'C)66', 'D)70', 'E)74']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the dimensions of the rectangular yard and then calculate the amount of fencing required for three sides.

1. **Identify the dimensions of the yard:**
- We know from fact1 that one side of the yard is 10 meters (unfenced side).
- From fact2, the area of the yard is 240 square meters.

2. **Calculate the other dimension:**
- Let the length of the unfenced side be \( l = 10 \) meters.
- Let the width of the yard be \( w \).
- The area of the rectangle is given by the formula:
\[
\text{Area} = l \times w = 240 \text{ square meters}
\]
- Substitute the known length:
\[
10 \times w = 240
\]
- Solve for \( w \):
\[
w = \frac{240}{10} = 24 \text{ meters}
\]

3. **Calculate the amount of fencing needed:**
- The fencing is required for three sides: two widths and one length.
- The total length of fencing required is:
\[
\text{Fencing} = 2w + l = 2(24) + 10
\]
- Calculate:
\[
\text{Fencing} = 48 + 10 = 58 \text{ meters}
\]

4. **Select the correct answer:**
- The amount of fencing needed is 58 meters.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: The sum of the digits of a three digit number is 17, and the sum of the squares of its digits is 109. If we subtract 495 from the number, we shall get a number consisting of the same digits written in the reverse order. Find the number. # Answer option: ['A)368', 'B)377', 'C)288', 'D)997', 'E)112']
To solve this problem, let's denote the three-digit number as \( \overline{abc} \), where \( a, b, \) and \( c \) are the digits of the number. Therefore, the number can be expressed as \( 100a + 10b + c \).

We have the following conditions from the problem:

1. The sum of the digits is 17:
\[
a + b + c = 17
\]

2. The sum of the squares of the digits is 109:
\[
a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109
\]

3. If we subtract 495 from the number, we get the number with its digits reversed:
\[
100a + 10b + c - 495 = 100c + 10b + a
\]

Simplifying this equation:
\[
100a + 10b + c - 495 = 100c + 10b + a
\]
\[
99a - 99c = 495
\]
\[
a - c = 5
\]

Now, we have three equations:
1. \( a + b + c = 17 \)
2. \( a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 109 \)
3. \( a - c = 5 \)

From equation 3, we can express \( a \) in terms of \( c \):
\[
a = c + 5
\]

Substitute \( a = c + 5 \) into equation 1:
\[
(c + 5) + b + c = 17
\]
\[
2c + b = 12
\]
\[
b = 12 - 2c
\]

Substitute \( a = c + 5 \) and \( b = 12 - 2c \) into equation 2:
\[
(c + 5)^2 + (12 - 2c)^2 + c^2 = 109
\]

Expanding each term:
\[
(c^2 + 10c + 25) + (144 - 48c + 4c^2) + c^2 = 109
\]

Combine like terms:
\[
6c^2 - 38c + 169 = 109
\]

Simplify:
\[
6c^2 - 38c + 60 = 0
\]

Divide the entire equation by 2:
\[
3c^2 - 19c + 30 = 0
\]

Now, solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:
\[
c = \frac{-b \pm \sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}
\]
where \( a = 3 \), \( b = -19 \), and \( c = 30 \).

Calculate the discriminant:
\[
b^2 - 4ac = (-19)^2 - 4 \times 3 \times 30 = 361 - 360 = 1
\]

The roots are:
\[
c = \frac{19 \pm 1}{6}
\]

This gives:
\[
c = \frac{20}{6} = \frac{10}{3} \quad \text{(not an integer, discard)}
\]
\[
c = \frac{18}{6} = 3
\]

So, \( c = 3 \).

Substitute \( c = 3 \) back to find \( a \) and \( b \):
\[
a = c + 5 = 3 + 5 = 8
\]
\[
b = 12 - 2c = 12 - 6 = 6
\]

Thus, the number is \( \overline{abc} = 863 \).

Question: A computer routine was developed to generate two numbers (x,y) the first being a random number between 0 and 100 inclusive, and the second being less than or equal to the square root of the first. Each of the following pair satisfies the routine except # Answer option: ['A)(99,10)', 'B)(85,9)', 'C)(50,7)', 'D)(1,1)', 'E)(1,0)']
To determine which pair does not satisfy the routine, we need to check each pair against the conditions given:

1. The first number \( x \) must be a random number between 0 and 100 inclusive.
2. The second number \( y \) must be less than or equal to the square root of the first number \( x \).

Let's evaluate each option:

- **Option A: (99, 10)**
- \( x = 99 \), which is between 0 and 100, so it satisfies the first condition.
- The square root of 99 is approximately 9.95. Since \( y = 10 \) is greater than 9.95, it does not satisfy the second condition.

- **Option B: (85, 9)**
- \( x = 85 \), which is between 0 and 100, so it satisfies the first condition.
- The square root of 85 is approximately 9.22. Since \( y = 9 \) is less than 9.22, it satisfies the second condition.

- **Option C: (50, 7)**
- \( x = 50 \), which is between 0 and 100, so it satisfies the first condition.
- The square root of 50 is approximately 7.07. Since \( y = 7 \) is less than 7.07, it satisfies the second condition.

- **Option D: (1, 1)**
- \( x = 1 \), which is between 0 and 100, so it satisfies the first condition.
- The square root of 1 is 1. Since \( y = 1 \) is equal to 1, it satisfies the second condition.

- **Option E: (1, 0)**
- \( x = 1 \), which is between 0 and 100, so it satisfies the first condition.
- The square root of 1 is 1. Since \( y = 0 \) is less than 1, it satisfies the second condition.

The only pair that does not satisfy the routine is Option A, because the second number is greater than the square root of the first number.

Final answer: {A}

Question: At the end of his one-year investment, Charles received $54,080, including interest and principal from a certain investment. If the investment paid an annual interest of 8 percent compounded semi-annually, which of the following is the amount of money that Charles originally invested? # Answer option: ['A)$45,000', 'B)$50,000', 'C)$54,000', 'D)$59,000', 'E)$62,000']
To determine the amount of money Charles originally invested, we need to use the formula for compound interest. The formula for compound interest is:

\[ A = P \left(1 + \frac{r}{n}\right)^{nt} \]

where:
- \( A \) is the amount of money accumulated after n years, including interest.
- \( P \) is the principal amount (the initial amount of money).
- \( r \) is the annual interest rate (decimal).
- \( n \) is the number of times that interest is compounded per year.
- \( t \) is the time the money is invested for in years.

Given:
- \( A = 54,080 \)
- \( r = 8\% = 0.08 \)
- \( n = 2 \) (since the interest is compounded semi-annually)
- \( t = 1 \) year

We need to find \( P \).

Plug the known values into the formula:

\[ 54,080 = P \left(1 + \frac{0.08}{2}\right)^{2 \times 1} \]

Simplify the expression inside the parentheses:

\[ 54,080 = P \left(1 + 0.04\right)^2 \]

\[ 54,080 = P (1.04)^2 \]

Calculate \( (1.04)^2 \):

\[ (1.04)^2 = 1.0816 \]

Now, substitute back into the equation:

\[ 54,080 = P \times 1.0816 \]

Solve for \( P \):

\[ P = \frac{54,080}{1.0816} \]

Calculate \( P \):

\[ P \approx 50,000 \]

Therefore, the amount of money that Charles originally invested is approximately $50,000.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: The average weight of 10 oarsmen in a boat is increased by 1.8 kg when one of the crew, who weighs 53 kg is replaced by a new man. Find the weight of the new man. # Answer option: ['A)71', 'B)62', 'C)43', 'D)67', 'E)40']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the weight of the new man who replaced one of the oarsmen.

1. **Understand the change in average weight:**
- The average weight of the 10 oarsmen increased by 1.8 kg.
- This means the total weight of the 10 oarsmen increased by \(10 \times 1.8 = 18\) kg.

2. **Identify the weight of the replaced oarsman:**
- The oarsman who was replaced weighed 53 kg.

3. **Calculate the weight of the new man:**
- Let the weight of the new man be \(x\) kg.
- The increase in total weight due to the replacement is 18 kg.
- Therefore, the equation is:
\[
x - 53 = 18
\]
- Solving for \(x\):
\[
x = 18 + 53 = 71
\]

Thus, the weight of the new man is 71 kg.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: A straight picket fence is composed of x pickets each of which is 1/2 inch wide. If there are 6 inches of space between each pair of pickets, which of the following represents the length of fence in feet? # Answer option: ['A)13x/2', 'B)13x/2 - 6', 'C)13x/24', 'D)(13x+1)/24', 'E)(13x-12)/24']
To determine the total length of the fence in feet, we need to consider both the width of the pickets and the spaces between them.

1. **Width of the Pickets:**
- Each picket is 1/2 inch wide.
- For \( x \) pickets, the total width of the pickets is \( \frac{x}{2} \) inches.

2. **Spaces Between Pickets:**
- There are 6 inches of space between each pair of pickets.
- If there are \( x \) pickets, there will be \( x - 1 \) spaces between them.
- Therefore, the total space between the pickets is \( 6(x - 1) \) inches.

3. **Total Length in Inches:**
- The total length of the fence in inches is the sum of the total width of the pickets and the total space between them:
\[
\text{Total length in inches} = \frac{x}{2} + 6(x - 1)
\]
\[
= \frac{x}{2} + 6x - 6
\]
\[
= \frac{x}{2} + \frac{12x}{2} - \frac{12}{2}
\]
\[
= \frac{x + 12x - 12}{2}
\]
\[
= \frac{13x - 12}{2}
\]

4. **Convert to Feet:**
- Since there are 12 inches in a foot, we convert the total length from inches to feet by dividing by 12:
\[
\text{Total length in feet} = \frac{13x - 12}{2 \times 12}
\]
\[
= \frac{13x - 12}{24}
\]

Thus, the expression that represents the length of the fence in feet is \(\frac{13x - 12}{24}\).

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: On a map, the length of the road from Town F to Town G is measured to be 20 inches. On this map, 1/4 inch represents an actual distance of 10 miles. What is the actual distance, in miles, from Town F to Town G along this road? # Answer option: ['A)800', 'B)720', 'C)960', 'D)1140', 'E)1160']
To find the actual distance from Town F to Town G, we need to use the scale provided in the map.

1. **Understand the scale**: According to fact2, 1/4 inch on the map represents an actual distance of 10 miles.

2. **Determine how many 1/4 inches are in 20 inches**:
- Since 1 inch is equal to 4 quarters (1/4 inches), 20 inches is equal to \( 20 \times 4 = 80 \) quarters (1/4 inches).

3. **Calculate the actual distance**:
- Each 1/4 inch represents 10 miles, so 80 quarters (1/4 inches) will represent \( 80 \times 10 = 800 \) miles.

Therefore, the actual distance from Town F to Town G is 800 miles.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a
Question: A car finishes a journey in 20 hours at the speed of 60 km/hr. If the same distance is to be covered in 10 hours, how much speed does the car gain? # Answer option: ['A)80 kmph', 'B)50 kmph', 'C)120 kmph', 'D)70 kmph', 'E)80 kmph']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the distance of the journey and then calculate the speed required to cover that distance in a shorter time.

1. **Calculate the distance of the journey:**
- We know the car finishes the journey in 20 hours at a speed of 60 km/hr.
- Distance = Speed × Time
- Distance = 60 km/hr × 20 hours = 1200 km

2. **Determine the speed needed to cover the same distance in 10 hours:**
- We need to cover 1200 km in 10 hours.
- Speed = Distance / Time
- Speed = 1200 km / 10 hours = 120 km/hr

3. **Calculate the speed gain:**
- The original speed was 60 km/hr.
- The new speed is 120 km/hr.
- Speed gain = New speed - Original speed
- Speed gain = 120 km/hr - 60 km/hr = 60 km/hr

4. **Check the answer options:**
- The options given are: ['A)80 kmph', 'B)50 kmph', 'C)120 kmph', 'D)70 kmph', 'E)80 kmph']
- None of the options directly match the calculated speed gain of 60 km/hr.

It seems there might be an error in the options provided, as none of them match the calculated speed gain. However, based on the calculation, the speed gain should be 60 km/hr.

Final answer: {None of the options match the calculated speed gain of 60 km/hr}
Final Answer: n
Ground Truth Answer: c
Question: A merchant receives an invoice for a motor boat for $20 000 with terms 4/30, n/100. What is the highest simple interest rate at which he can afford to borrow money in order to take advantage of the discount? # Answer option: ['A)247.67', 'B)237.67', 'C)227.67', 'D)215.67', 'E)None of these']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the highest simple interest rate at which the merchant can afford to borrow money to take advantage of the discount offered by the invoice terms.

1. **Understanding the Invoice Terms:**
- The invoice amount is $20,000.
- The terms are 4/30, n/100. This means a 4% discount is available if the invoice is paid within 30 days; otherwise, the net amount is due in 100 days.

2. **Calculating the Discount:**
- A 4% discount on $20,000 is calculated as follows:
\[
\text{Discount} = 0.04 \times 20,000 = 800
\]
- Therefore, if the merchant pays within 30 days, he only needs to pay:
\[
20,000 - 800 = 19,200
\]

3. **Interest Calculation:**
- The merchant can save $800 by paying early. To take advantage of this, he might consider borrowing $19,200 for 70 days (the difference between 100 days and 30 days).

4. **Simple Interest Formula:**
- The simple interest formula is:
\[
\text{Interest} = \text{Principal} \times \text{Rate} \times \text{Time}
\]
- Here, the interest saved is $800, the principal is $19,200, and the time is 70 days (expressed as a fraction of a year: \(\frac{70}{365}\)).

Question: Car ‘X’ covers a distance of 320 kms in 8 hours and car ‘Y’ covers a distance of 415 kms in 5 hrs. What is the difference in the speed of the two cars? # Answer option: ['A)42kms/hr', 'B)41km/hr', 'C)43kms/hr', 'D)45kms/hr', 'E)None of these']
To find the difference in the speed of the two cars, we need to calculate the speed of each car first and then find the difference between these speeds.

**Step 1: Calculate the speed of Car 'X'.**

Given:
- Distance covered by Car 'X' = 320 km
- Time taken by Car 'X' = 8 hours

Speed of Car 'X' = Distance / Time = 320 km / 8 hours = 40 km/hr

**Step 2: Calculate the speed of Car 'Y'.**

Given:
- Distance covered by Car 'Y' = 415 km
- Time taken by Car 'Y' = 5 hours

Speed of Car 'Y' = Distance / Time = 415 km / 5 hours = 83 km/hr

**Step 3: Calculate the difference in speed between Car 'Y' and Car 'X'.**

Difference in speed = Speed of Car 'Y' - Speed of Car 'X' = 83 km/hr - 40 km/hr = 43 km/hr

Therefore, the difference in the speed of the two cars is 43 km/hr.

Question: A coin made of alloy of aluminum and silver measures 2 x 15 mm. If the weight of the coin is 30 grams and the volume of aluminum in the alloy equals that of silver, what will be the weight of a coin measuring 1 x 30 mm made of pure aluminum if silver is twice as heavy as aluminum? # Answer option: ['A)36 grams', 'B)40 grams', 'C)42 grams', 'D)48 grams', 'E)50 grams']
To solve this problem, we need to analyze the given information and apply it to find the weight of a coin made of pure aluminum.

1. **Understanding the Original Coin:**
- The original coin is made of an alloy of aluminum and silver.
- The dimensions of the original coin are 2 x 15 mm.
- The weight of the original coin is 30 grams.
- The volume of aluminum in the alloy equals that of silver.
- Silver is twice as heavy as aluminum.

2. **Volume and Weight Analysis:**
- Since the volume of aluminum equals the volume of silver, let's denote the volume of each as \( V \).
- The total volume of the coin is \( 2V \).
- Let the density of aluminum be \( \rho_A \) and the density of silver be \( \rho_S \).
- Given that silver is twice as heavy as aluminum, \( \rho_S = 2\rho_A \).

3. **Weight Calculation of the Original Coin:**
- The weight of the aluminum part is \( V \cdot \rho_A \).
- The weight of the silver part is \( V \cdot \rho_S = V \cdot 2\rho_A \).
- The total weight of the coin is \( V \cdot \rho_A + V \cdot 2\rho_A = 3V \cdot \rho_A \).
- We know this total weight is 30 grams, so \( 3V \cdot \rho_A = 30 \).
- Solving for \( V \cdot \rho_A \), we get \( V \cdot \rho_A = 10 \).

4. **New Coin Analysis:**
- The new coin is made of pure aluminum and measures 1 x 30 mm.
- The volume of the new coin is the same as the original coin because \( 2 \times 15 = 1 \times 30 \).
- Therefore, the volume of the new coin is \( 2V \).

5. **Weight Calculation of the New Coin:**
- Since the new coin is made of pure aluminum, its weight is \( 2V \cdot \rho_A \).
- We know \( V \cdot \rho_A = 10 \), so \( 2V \cdot \rho_A = 2 \times 10 = 20 \).

Thus, the weight of the new coin made of pure aluminum is 20 grams. However, it seems there is a discrepancy because none of the answer options match this result. Let's re-evaluate the options:

- The options provided are: ['A)36 grams', 'B)40 grams', 'C)42 grams', 'D)48 grams', 'E)50 grams'].

However, based on the logical steps and calculations, the weight of the new coin should be 20 grams, which is not listed in the options. Therefore, there might be an error in the problem statement or options provided.

Final answer: {None of the options match the calculated result of 20 grams.}

Question: Janice bikes at 10 miles per hour, while Jennie bikes at 20. How long until they have collectively biked 1 mile? # Answer option: ['A)1 minute', 'B)2 minutes', 'C)3 minutes', 'D)4 minutes', 'E)5 minutes']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how long it takes for Janice and Jennie to collectively bike 1 mile.

1. **Determine the rate at which each person bikes:**
- Janice bikes at 10 miles per hour.
- Jennie bikes at 20 miles per hour.

2. **Calculate the combined rate:**
- The combined rate is the sum of their individual rates:
\[
10 \text{ miles per hour} + 20 \text{ miles per hour} = 30 \text{ miles per hour}
\]

3. **Determine how long it takes to bike 1 mile at the combined rate:**
- If they bike at a combined rate of 30 miles per hour, we need to find the time it takes to bike 1 mile.
- Time is calculated as distance divided by rate. Therefore, the time to bike 1 mile is:
\[
\text{Time} = \frac{1 \text{ mile}}{30 \text{ miles per hour}} = \frac{1}{30} \text{ hours}
\]

4. **Convert the time from hours to minutes:**
- Since there are 60 minutes in an hour, we convert \(\frac{1}{30}\) hours to minutes:
\[
\frac{1}{30} \text{ hours} \times 60 \text{ minutes per hour} = 2 \text{ minutes}
\]

Thus, it takes 2 minutes for Janice and Jennie to collectively bike 1 mile.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b

To determine the number of ways to arrange the books on a shelf, we need to calculate the number of permutations of the books. Since there are six different books, we can use the formula for permutations of n distinct items, which is n! (n factorial).

2. Calculate the factorial of the number of books:

\]
\[
30 \times 4 = 120
\]
\[
120 \times 3 = 360
\]
\[
360 \times 2 = 720
\]
\[
720 \times 1 = 720

- E) Cannot be determined

Question: A father wants to divide Rs. 5100 between his two sons, Mohan and Sohan who are 23 and 24 at present. He divides the amount in such a way that if their shares are invested at compound interest at 4% p.a. they will receive equal amount on attaining the age of 26 years. Find Mohan's share. # Answer option: ['A)2400', 'B)2500', 'C)2600', 'D)2700', 'E)None of these']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the shares of Mohan and Sohan such that when invested at a compound interest rate of 4% per annum, they will have equal amounts when they both reach the age of 26.

1. **Determine the time period for investment:**
- Mohan is currently 23 years old, so he will invest his share for 3 years (26 - 23 = 3).
- Sohan is currently 24 years old, so he will invest his share for 2 years (26 - 24 = 2).

2. **Let Mohan's share be Rs. x.**
- Then, Sohan's share will be Rs. (5100 - x).

3. **Calculate the future value of Mohan's share:**
- The future value of Mohan's share after 3 years at 4% compound interest is given by:
\[
\text{Future Value of Mohan's share} = x \times \left(1 + \frac{4}{100}\right)^3 = x \times (1.04)^3
\]

4. **Calculate the future value of Sohan's share:**
- The future value of Sohan's share after 2 years at 4% compound interest is given by:
\[
\text{Future Value of Sohan's share} = (5100 - x) \times \left(1 + \frac{4}{100}\right)^2 = (5100 - x) \times (1.04)^2
\]

5. **Set the future values equal to each other:**
\[
x \times (1.04)^3 = (5100 - x) \times (1.04)^2
\]

6. **Simplify and solve for x:**
- Divide both sides by \((1.04)^2\):
\[
x \times 1.04 = 5100 - x
\]
- Simplify the equation:
\[
x \times 1.04 + x = 5100
\]
\[
2.04x = 5100
\]
- Solve for x:
\[
x = \frac{5100}{2.04} = 2500
\]

Therefore, Mohan's share is Rs. 2500.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b

Question: Two friends are eating a jar full of candies. Had P eaten alone, it would have taken him 10 minutes to finish the candies in the jar. Had Q eaten alone, it would have taken her 5 minutes to finish half the jar. Since both of them are eating simultaneously, how many minutes would it take them to empty the jar? # Answer option: ['A)4', 'B)5', 'C)6', 'D)7', 'E)8']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the combined rate at which P and Q can eat the candies and then calculate the time it takes for them to finish the entire jar together.

**Step 1: Determine P's rate of eating candies.**

From fact 1, we know that P can finish the entire jar in 10 minutes. Therefore, P's rate of eating is:
\[ \text{Rate of P} = \frac{1 \text{ jar}}{10 \text{ minutes}} = \frac{1}{10} \text{ jar per minute} \]

**Step 2: Determine Q's rate of eating candies.**

From fact 2, we know that Q can finish half the jar in 5 minutes. Therefore, Q's rate of eating is:
\[ \text{Rate of Q} = \frac{0.5 \text{ jar}}{5 \text{ minutes}} = \frac{1}{10} \text{ jar per minute} \]

**Step 3: Determine the combined rate of P and Q.**

Since P and Q are eating simultaneously, we add their rates together to find their combined rate:
\[ \text{Combined rate} = \text{Rate of P} + \text{Rate of Q} = \frac{1}{10} + \frac{1}{10} = \frac{2}{10} = \frac{1}{5} \text{ jar per minute} \]

**Step 4: Calculate the time taken to finish the jar together.**

To find the time it takes for them to finish the entire jar together, we use the formula:
\[ \text{Time} = \frac{\text{Total work (1 jar)}}{\text{Combined rate}} = \frac{1 \text{ jar}}{\frac{1}{5} \text{ jar per minute}} = 5 \text{ minutes} \]

Therefore, it would take P and Q 5 minutes to empty the jar when eating together.

Final answer: {B}
Final Answer: b
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: Tires of a certain brand, when purchased new, last for four years. A customer can choose to purchase the new tires at a cost of $180 per tire or can have his current tires repaired at a cost of $40 per tire, a repair that will make the current tires last for one additional year. The average cost per year of the new tires is what percent greater than the cost of repairing the current tires? # Answer option: ['A)8%', 'B)10%', 'C)12.5%', 'D)16.7%', 'E)25%']
To solve this problem, we need to calculate the average cost per year for both purchasing new tires and repairing the current tires, and then determine the percentage difference between these two costs.

1. **Calculate the average cost per year for new tires:**

- The cost of new tires is $180 per tire.
- New tires last for 4 years.
- Therefore, the average cost per year for new tires is:
\[
\text{Average cost per year for new tires} = \frac{\$180}{4} = \$45
\]

2. **Calculate the average cost per year for repairing current tires:**

- The cost of repairing current tires is $40 per tire.
- Repairs make the tires last for 1 additional year.
- Therefore, the average cost per year for repairing tires is:
\[
\text{Average cost per year for repairing tires} = \$40
\]

3. **Calculate the percentage difference:**

- The difference in average cost per year between new tires and repaired tires is:
\[
\$45 - \$40 = \$5
\]
- To find the percentage difference relative to the cost of repairing tires, we use the formula:
\[
\text{Percentage difference} = \left(\frac{\text{Difference}}{\text{Cost of repairing tires}}\right) \times 100\%
\]
- Substituting the values, we get:
\[
\text{Percentage difference} = \left(\frac{5}{40}\right) \times 100\% = 12.5\%
\]

Therefore, the average cost per year of the new tires is 12.5% greater than the cost of repairing the current tires.

Final answer: {C}
Final Answer: c
Ground Truth Answer: c

Question: Two ants are moving from their farms towards each other. Ant A is moving at a speed of 9 cm per hour and ant B is moving at a speed of 6 cm per hour. If the farms are 75 cm away from each other, what will be the distance (in cm) that ant A travels until meeting ant B? # Answer option: ['A)45', 'B)48', 'C)51', 'D)54', 'E)57']
To solve this problem, we need to determine how far Ant A travels before meeting Ant B. We know the following:

- Ant A's speed is 9 cm per hour.
- Ant B's speed is 6 cm per hour.
- The total distance between the two farms is 75 cm.

First, we calculate the combined speed of both ants as they move towards each other:

\[
\text{Combined speed} = \text{Speed of Ant A} + \text{Speed of Ant B} = 9 \, \text{cm/hour} + 6 \, \text{cm/hour} = 15 \, \text{cm/hour}
\]

Next, we determine the time it takes for the ants to meet. Since they are moving towards each other, they will cover the entire distance between the farms together. Therefore, the time taken to meet is:

\[
\text{Time to meet} = \frac{\text{Total distance}}{\text{Combined speed}} = \frac{75 \, \text{cm}}{15 \, \text{cm/hour}} = 5 \, \text{hours}
\]

Now, we calculate the distance that Ant A travels in this time. Since Ant A travels at 9 cm per hour, the distance it covers in 5 hours is:

\[
\text{Distance traveled by Ant A} = \text{Speed of Ant A} \times \text{Time to meet} = 9 \, \text{cm/hour} \times 5 \, \text{hours} = 45 \, \text{cm}
\]

Therefore, the distance that Ant A travels until meeting Ant B is 45 cm.

Final answer: {A}
Final Answer: a
Ground Truth Answer: a

- Fixed monthly salary: 1500 Rupees
- Commission on sales: 15% of the monthly sales

- Total monthly income = Fixed salary + Commission on sales
- We want the total monthly income to be 6000 Rupees.

- Let \( S \) be the monthly sales in Rupees.

\[

\]

\[
0.15S = 6000 - 1500
\]
\[
0.15S = 4500
\]

\[
S = \frac{4500}{0.15}
\]
\[
S = 30000
\]

Question: At a conference, one team is made up of 4 men and 4 women. Four presenters are chosen to present the team's findings in front of the entire conference. How many different groups of presenters can be chosen from the team if a team cannot be composed of men only or women only? (Two groups of presenters are considered different if at least one presenter is different.)
To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of different groups of 4 presenters that can be chosen from a team of 4 men and 4 women, with the condition that the group cannot be composed entirely of men or entirely of women.

Let's break down the solution step by step:

1. **Total number of ways to choose 4 presenters from 8 people (4 men and 4 women):**

We can use the combination formula to calculate this:
\[
\binom{8}{4} = \frac{8 \times 7 \times 6 \times 5}{4 \times 3 \times 2 \times 1} = 70
\]

2. **Number of ways to choose 4 men only:**

Since there are 4 men, the number of ways to choose all 4 men is:
\[
\binom{4}{4} = 1
\]

3. **Number of ways to choose 4 women only:**

Similarly, since there are 4 women, the number of ways to choose all 4 women is:
\[
\binom{4}{4} = 1
\]

4. **Subtract the invalid groups (all men or all women):**

We need to subtract the cases where the group is composed entirely of men or entirely of women from the total number of ways to choose 4 presenters:
\[
70 - 1 - 1 = 68
\]

Therefore, the number of different groups of presenters that can be chosen, ensuring that the group is not composed entirely of men or entirely of women, is 68.

Final answer: {68}
Final Answer: 6
Ground Truth Answer: b
Question: Of the 200 students in a school, at least 45% attended the prom night and at least 35% took part in the debating session. What is the maximum number of students who could have neither attended the prom night nor the debating session? # Answer option: ['A)27', 'B)81', 'C)90', 'D)99', 'E)110']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the maximum number of students who could have neither attended the prom night nor participated in the debating session.

1. **Calculate the number of students who attended the prom night:**
- According to fact2, at least 45% of the 200 students attended the prom night.
- 45% of 200 is calculated as follows:
\[
0.45 \times 200 = 90
\]
- Therefore, at least 90 students attended the prom night.

2. **Calculate the number of students who participated in the debating session:**
- According to fact3, at least 35% of the 200 students took part in the debating session.
- 35% of 200 is calculated as follows:
\[
0.35 \times 200 = 70
\]
- Therefore, at least 70 students participated in the debating session.

3. **Determine the minimum number of students who attended either the prom night or the debating session or both:**
- To find the minimum number of students who attended at least one of the events, we use the principle of inclusion-exclusion.
- Let \( P \) be the set of students who attended the prom night, and \( D \) be the set of students who participated in the debating session.
- The minimum number of students who attended at least one event is given by:
\[
|P \cup D| = |P| + |D| - |P \cap D|
\]
- We want to maximize the number of students who attended neither event, which means minimizing \( |P \cup D| \).
- The minimum value of \( |P \cup D| \) occurs when the overlap \( |P \cap D| \) is maximized.
- The maximum possible overlap is when all students in the smaller group (debating session) are also in the larger group (prom night), i.e., \( |P \cap D| = 70 \).

4. **Calculate the minimum number of students who attended at least one event:**
- Substitute the values into the inclusion-exclusion formula:
\[
|P \cup D| = 90 + 70 - 70 = 90
\]
- Therefore, at least 90 students attended at least one of the events.

5. **Calculate the maximum number of students who attended neither event:**
- The total number of students is 200.
- The maximum number of students who attended neither event is:
\[
200 - |P \cup D| = 200 - 90 = 110
\]

Thus, the maximum number of students who could have neither attended the prom night nor the debating session is 110.

Final answer: {E}
Final Answer: e
Ground Truth Answer: e
Question: If one third of 3/4 of a number is 21. Then, find the number? # Answer option: ['A)84', 'B)66', 'C)28', 'D)19', 'E)11']
To solve the problem, we need to find the original number based on the given fact: "one third of 3/4 of a number is 21."

Let's break it down step by step:

1. **Let the number be \( x \).**

2. **Calculate 3/4 of the number:**
\[
\frac{3}{4} \times x
\]

3. **Calculate one third of the result from step 2:**
\[
\frac{1}{3} \times \left(\frac{3}{4} \times x\right) = \frac{3}{4} \times \frac{1}{3} \times x = \frac{1}{4} \times x
\]

4. **Set the expression equal to 21, as given in the fact:**
\[
\frac{1}{4} \times x = 21
\]

5. **Solve for \( x \):**
\[
x = 21 \times 4 = 84
\]

Thus, the original number is 84.

Question: A cyclist travels at 12 miles per hour. How many minutes will it take to travel 48 miles?
To determine how many minutes it will take for the cyclist to travel 48 miles at a speed of 12 miles per hour, we can follow these steps:

1. **Calculate the time in hours:**
- The formula to calculate time is:
\[
\text{Time} = \frac{\text{Distance}}{\text{Speed}}
\]
- Here, the distance is 48 miles and the speed is 12 miles per hour.
- Plugging in the values:
\[
\text{Time} = \frac{48 \text{ miles}}{12 \text{ miles per hour}} = 4 \text{ hours}
\]

2. **Convert hours to minutes:**
- There are 60 minutes in an hour.
- Therefore, to convert 4 hours into minutes:
\[
4 \text{ hours} \times 60 \text{ minutes per hour} = 240 \text{ minutes}
\]

Thus, it will take the cyclist 240 minutes to travel 48 miles at a speed of 12 miles per hour.

Question: Last year, a Home Appliance Store sold an average(arithmetic mean) of 42 microwave ovens per month. In the first 10 months of this year, the store has sold an average(arithmetic mean) of only 20 microwave ovens per month. What was the average number of microwave ovens sold per month during the entire 22 months period? # Answer option: ['A)21', 'B)30', 'C)31', 'D)32', 'E)None of the above']
To find the average number of microwave ovens sold per month over the entire 22-month period, we need to calculate the total number of microwave ovens sold during this period and then divide by the total number of months.

1. **Calculate the total number of microwave ovens sold last year:**
- Last year, the store sold an average of 42 microwave ovens per month.
- There are 12 months in a year.
- Total sold last year = 42 ovens/month * 12 months = 504 ovens.

2. **Calculate the total number of microwave ovens sold in the first 10 months of this year:**
- This year, the store sold an average of 20 microwave ovens per month for the first 10 months.
- Total sold in the first 10 months = 20 ovens/month * 10 months = 200 ovens.

3. **Calculate the total number of microwave ovens sold over the entire 22-month period:**
- Total sold over 22 months = Total sold last year + Total sold in the first 10 months of this year
- Total sold over 22 months = 504 ovens + 200 ovens = 704 ovens.

4. **Calculate the average number of microwave ovens sold per month over the 22-month period:**
- Average = Total sold over 22 months / Total number of months
- Average = 704 ovens / 22 months ≈ 32 ovens/month.

Therefore, the average number of microwave ovens sold per month during the entire 22-month period is 32.

Final answer: {D}

Ground Truth Answer: d
Question: John likes to have lightly flavored tea every evening. In a 50% strong milk tea, he replaces 15% of it with milk twice. Then, he replaces 10 percent of the resultant solution with more milk. What is the final concentration of tea John drinks? # Answer option: ['A)15.38%', 'B)42%', 'C)39.86%', 'D)22.35%', 'E)32.51%']
To solve this problem, we need to calculate the concentration of tea after each step of replacing a portion of the solution with milk.

1. **Initial Concentration:**
- The initial concentration of tea is 50%.

2. **First Replacement:**
- John replaces 15% of the 50% strong milk tea with milk.
- The amount of tea in the original solution is 50%.
- After replacing 15% of the solution with milk (which has 0% tea), the new concentration of tea is:
\[
\text{New concentration} = 50\% \times (1 - 0.15) = 50\% \times 0.85 = 42.5\%
\]

3. **Second Replacement:**
- John again replaces 15% of the new solution (42.5% tea) with milk.
- The new concentration of tea is:
\[
\text{New concentration} = 42.5\% \times (1 - 0.15) = 42.5\% \times 0.85 = 36.125\%
\]

4. **Third Replacement:**
- John replaces 10% of the resultant solution (36.125% tea) with milk.
- The final concentration of tea is:
\[
\text{Final concentration} = 36.125\% \times (1 - 0.10) = 36.125\% \times 0.90 = 32.5125\%
\]

Therefore, the final concentration of tea that John drinks is approximately 32.51%.

To determine the total number of ways to travel from place M to place Q, we need to consider the number of bus options available for each segment of the journey and multiply them together.

1. **Travel from M to N:**
- There are 3 buses available for this segment.

2. **Travel from N to O:**
- There are 4 buses available for this segment.

3. **Travel from O to P:**
- There is 1 bus available for this segment.

4. **Travel from P to Q:**
- There are 3 buses available for this segment.

To find the total number of ways to travel from M to Q, we multiply the number of options for each segment:

\[
3 \text{ (buses from M to N)} \times 4 \text{ (buses from N to O)} \times 1 \text{ (bus from O to P)} \times 3 \text{ (buses from P to Q)} = 36
\]

Thus, the total number of ways to travel from M to Q is 36.

Question: The monthly salary S of a shop assistant is the sum of a fixed salary of $500 plus 5% of all monthly sales. What should the monthly sales be so that her monthly salary reaches $1500?
To determine the monthly sales required for the shop assistant's salary to reach $1500, we need to break down the components of her salary and set up an equation based on the given facts.

1. **Fixed Salary Component**: The shop assistant has a fixed salary of $500 per month. This is a constant amount that does not change with sales.

2. **Commission Component**: The shop assistant earns 5% of all monthly sales. If we let \( x \) represent the monthly sales, then the commission earned from sales is \( 0.05x \).

3. **Total Monthly Salary**: The total monthly salary \( S \) is the sum of the fixed salary and the commission from sales. Therefore, the equation for the total salary is:
\[
S = 500 + 0.05x
\]

4. **Desired Salary**: We want the total monthly salary to be $1500. So, we set up the equation:
\[
1500 = 500 + 0.05x
\]

5. **Solve for \( x \)**: To find the value of \( x \) (the monthly sales), we need to solve the equation:
\[
1500 = 500 + 0.05x
\]

Subtract 500 from both sides:
\[
1500 - 500 = 0.05x
\]
\[
1000 = 0.05x
\]

Divide both sides by 0.05 to solve for \( x \):
\[
x = \frac{1000}{0.05}
\]
\[
x = 20000
\]

Therefore, the monthly sales should be \(\$20,000\) for the shop assistant's salary to reach $1500.

Final answer: \{20000\}

To solve this problem, we need to determine how many sales of $250 each the salesperson must make to earn a commission that results in a salary of at least $1000.

1. **Understand the Commission Structure:**
- The salesperson earns a 10% commission on each sale.
- For a sale of $250, the commission is calculated as follows:
\[
\text{Commission per sale} = 10\% \times 250 = 0.10 \times 250 = 25
\]
- Therefore, the salesperson earns $25 for each sale of $250.

2. **Determine the Total Commission Needed:**
- The salesperson wants to earn at least $1000 in commission.
- Let \( x \) be the number of sales needed.
- The total commission from \( x \) sales is \( 25x \).

3. **Set Up the Inequality:**
- We need the total commission to be at least $1000:
\[
25x \geq 1000
\]

4. **Solve the Inequality:**
- Divide both sides by 25 to solve for \( x \):
\[
x \geq \frac{1000}{25} = 40
\]

5. **Conclusion:**
- The salesperson must make at least 40 sales to earn a commission of at least $1000.

Therefore, the correct answer is option D.

To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of red sweets in the bag given the ratio of red to green sweets and the number of green sweets.

\]

\[

Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization? # Answer option: ['A)300', 'B)200', 'C)400', 'D)100', 'E)500']
To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of employees in the organization based on the given facts.

Let's denote the number of employees as \( n \).

1. **Initial Contribution:**
- The total amount to be raised is Rs. 6 lakh.
- Each employee contributes an equal amount, so the contribution per employee is \( \frac{600000}{n} \).

2. **Increased Contribution:**
- If each employee contributes Rs. 60 extra, the total contribution becomes Rs. 6.24 lakh.
- The new contribution per employee is \( \frac{624000}{n} \).

3. **Setting up the Equation:**
- The increased contribution per employee is the initial contribution plus Rs. 60.
- Therefore, we have the equation:
\[
\frac{624000}{n} = \frac{600000}{n} + 60
\]

4. **Solving the Equation:**
- Subtract \( \frac{600000}{n} \) from both sides:
\[
\frac{624000}{n} - \frac{600000}{n} = 60
\]
- Simplify the left side:
\[
\frac{624000 - 600000}{n} = 60
\]
\[
\frac{24000}{n} = 60
\]
- Solve for \( n \):
\[
n = \frac{24000}{60}
\]
\[
n = 400
\]

Thus, the number of employees in the organization is 400.

Question: A shopkeeper in order to promote his new shop put a discount of 20% on all the items for one day. Now he must sell the items at original price the other day. By what percentage must he increase the price to original? # Answer option: ['A)21%', 'B)20%', 'C)25%', 'D)33%', 'E)18%']
To solve this problem, we need to determine by what percentage the discounted price must be increased to return to the original price.

Let's break it down step by step:

1. **Understanding the Discount**:
- The shopkeeper offers a 20% discount on all items.
- This means the selling price on the discount day is 80% of the original price (100% - 20% = 80%).

2. **Expressing the Discounted Price**:
- Let the original price of an item be \( P \).
- The discounted price is \( 0.8P \).

3. **Finding the Required Increase**:
- To return to the original price \( P \) from the discounted price \( 0.8P \), we need to find the percentage increase from \( 0.8P \) to \( P \).

4. **Calculating the Increase**:
- The increase needed is \( P - 0.8P = 0.2P \).
- The percentage increase is calculated as:
\[
\text{Percentage Increase} = \left(\frac{\text{Increase}}{\text{Original (Discounted) Price}}\right) \times 100\%
\]
- Substituting the values, we get:
\[
\text{Percentage Increase} = \left(\frac{0.2P}{0.8P}\right) \times 100\%
\]
- Simplifying, we have:
\[
\text{Percentage Increase} = \left(\frac{0.2}{0.8}\right) \times 100\% = 0.25 \times 100\% = 25\%
\]

Therefore, the price must be increased by 25% to return to the original price.

Final answer: {C}
